Evidence for the First Type of Istita'a: Ability of Means
Al-Nasafi cites four Quranic verses to prove istita'a means ability of means.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic evidence that establishes that istita'a (ability) in the Quran often refers to ability of means and instruments (istita'at al-asbab wa al-alat), not merely real power for the act.

Core Idea
The Quran uses istita'a to mean having means, not just power.

Islamic theologians debated whether istita'a (ability) refers to real power for an act or to external means. Al-Nasafi provides Quranic evidence that many verses refer to ability of means, such as health and provisions, not the power to perform the act itself. This lesson examines the key verses he cites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Al-Nasafi argues that istita'a is divided into two types, and he presents evidence from the Quran. Read the passage to understand the claim.
The claim is that istita'a can mean ability of means, not just real power.
2
Analyze the first verse (58:4)
Examine why the verse about expiation for zihar proves ability of means. Consider why it cannot refer to real power (qudra).
The verse mentions 'whoever does not have the ability' regarding fasting two months. Al-Nasafi argues that real power cannot exist before starting the act.
3
Analyze the hypocrites' verse (9:42)
Understand why Allah calling the hypocrites liars shows they meant ability of means, not real power. Note the distinction between real power and means.
If they meant real power, they would not be liars because real power for jihad does not persist from Medina to the battlefield.
4
Review additional verses (4:25, 3:97) and conclusion
See how the verses about marriage and pilgrimage also refer to means. Conclude that the Quran uses istita'a for ability of means.
These verses strengthen the argument that istita'a has a broader meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدليل على انقسام الاستطاعة إلى قسمين قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا ﴾ والمراد منه استطاعة الأسباب والآلات إذ لا يتصور وجود قدرة أداء صوم شهرين من قبل الشروع في أدائه، ويستحيل بقاء القدرة التي كانت موجودة عند الخصوم إلى شهرين، فدل أنه أراد به استطاعة سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات. والدليل عليه ما عير الله تعالى به من قال من أهل النفاق : ﴿ لَوِ اسْتَطَعْنَا لَخَرَجْنَا مَعَكُمْ ﴾ وكذبهم الله تعالى في ذلك القول، ولو كانوا أرادوا بذلك الكلام الاستطاعة التي هي حقيقة قدرة الفعل ما كانوا بنفيها عن أنفسهم كاذبين، إذ لا شك أن استطاعة فعل الجهاد لا تبقى من وقت كونهم بالمدينة إلى أن يلقوا العدو ويباشروا القتال، وكان الخروج مطلوبًا لذلك، وحيث كذبهم دل أنهم أرادوا بذلك المرض أو فقد المال على ما بين الله تعالى بقوله : ﴿ لَيْسَ عَلَى الضُّعَفَاءِ وَلَا عَلَى الْمَرْضَى ﴾ إلى أن قال: ﴿ إِنَّمَا السَّبِيلُ عَلَى الَّذِينَ يَسْتَذِنُونَكَ وَهُمْ أَغْنِياء ﴾ . يحققه أن أهل النفاق كانوا عوام، وقدرة العمل التي توجب حصول الفعل ويتكلم فيها المتكلمون أنها مع الفعل أو قبله وتبقى أو لا تبقى مما لا يعرفه العوام ولا يصورونها في الأوهام، وذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ مِنكُمْ طَوْلًا ﴾ والمراد به استطاعة الآلات، وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا ﴾ والمراد به الزاد والراحلة لا حقيقة قدرة الفعل، فهذه الآيات دليل ثبوت استطاعة الأسباب والآلات.
Then the evidence for the division of istita'a (ability) into two types is His statement, the Exalted: 'And whoever does not have the ability, then the feeding of sixty needy persons' (Quran 58:4). What is intended by it is the ability of means and instruments, because it is inconceivable that the power to perform fasting for two months exists before beginning its performance, and it is impossible for the power that existed according to the opponents to last for two months. So it indicates that He intended by it the ability of soundness of means and health of instruments. And the evidence for it is what Allah, the Exalted, rebuked those who said among the hypocrites: 'If we had the ability, we would have gone out with you' (Quran 9:42), and Allah declared them liars in that statement. If they had intended by that speech the ability which is the true power (haqiqat qudrat al-fi'l) of the act, they would not have been liars in denying it of themselves, because there is no doubt that the ability to perform jihad does not remain from the time they were in Medina until they meet the enemy and engage in battle, and going out was required for that. And since He declared them liars, it indicates that they intended by that illness or lack of wealth, as Allah, the Exalted, clarified by His statement: 'There is no blame upon the weak nor upon the sick' until He said: 'The way is only against those who ask permission of you while they are rich' (Quran 9:91-93). He confirms that the hypocrites were commoners, and the power of action that necessitates the occurrence of the act and the mutakallimun discuss whether it is with the act or before it and whether it remains or does not remain is something that the commoners do not know nor do they conceptualize in their minds. And that is His statement, the Exalted: 'And whoever among you does not have the means' (Quran 4:25); what is intended by it is the ability of instruments. Likewise His statement, the Exalted: 'And due to Allah from the people is pilgrimage to the House – for whoever has the ability to it a way' (Quran 3:97); what is intended by it is provisions and the mount, not the true power of the act. So these verses are evidence for the affirmation of the ability of means and instruments.
Source pages p. 787

Commentary
This passage is a proof-text argument for the existence of the first type of istita'a, namely istita'at al-asbab wa al-alat (ability of means and instruments). The author begins by stating that the evidence for the division of istita'a into two types is Quranic. The first verse cited is 58:4 (expiation for zihar), which mentions feeding sixty poor for one who 'does not have the ability' to fast two months. Al-Nasafi argues that this cannot refer to real power (qudra) because it is impossible for a person to have the power to fast two months before beginning; rather it refers to physical health and means. Similarly, the hypocrites' claim in 9:42 that they would have gone out for jihad if they had the ability is rejected by Allah. If they meant real power, they would not be liars because real power for jihad does not persist from Medina to the battlefield. Hence they meant health and wealth, as Allah clarifies in subsequent verses. The author adds that common people do not understand the technical discussions of mutakallimun about whether power is with the act or before it; thus the Quranic usage aligns with the common understanding. Finally, verses 4:25 (marriage) and 3:97 (pilgrimage) are also cited as referring to means, not real power. So these verses collectively prove the existence of ability of means and instruments.

Key Terms
استطاعة
قدرة
أسباب
آلات
استطاعة الأسباب والآلات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Quranic references to istita'a refer to real power (qudra) for the act.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that verses like Q58:4, Q9:42, Q4:25, Q3:97 refer to ability of means such as health and provisions, not real power.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does al-Nasafi cite first to prove that istita'a can mean ability of means?
A) Quran 9:42 (hypocrites' excuse)
B) Quran 58:4 (expiation for zihar)
C) Quran 11:20 (they cannot hear)
D) Quran 18:72 (Moses and Khidr)

Key Takeaway
The Quran uses istita'a to refer to ability of means in several key verses, supporting the Maturidi position on the two types of ability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I can't' to an act of worship, is it because you lack real ability (health, time, resources) or because you lack the genuine desire? How often do you confuse the two? Write down one excuse you made this week and examine its truth in light of this lesson.
?
The hypocrites claimed inability but Allah exposed their lie. Are there areas in your life where you claim you cannot obey Allah when in fact you have the means? What would it take for you to stop hiding behind invalid excuses? Commit to one specific action this week.
?
Al-Nasafi argues that the Quran's use of istita'a aligns with common understanding. When you read Quranic commands, do you interpret 'ability' as divine power or as your own physical and material capacity? How does this affect your sense of responsibility? Pray about one command you've been avoiding and ask for clear ability.

Quranic Evidence for Istita'a as Real Power
Al-Nasafi provides Quranic evidence for istita'a as real power (haqiqat al-qudra).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi uses Quranic verses to distinguish between two types of inability and to prove that real power (qudra) is distinct from means and instruments.

Core Idea
Real power is blameworthy when absent; lack of means is not.

Al-Nasafi now turns to textual evidence for the second type of istita'a—the real power by which acts are performed. He cites a key verse about disbelievers being unable to hear, and unpacks why this inability is blameworthy. The lesson shows how he argues that blame only attaches when means are present but real power is absent due to one's own negligence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the main proof. Notice how al-Nasafi cites Quran 11:20 and then explains its meaning.
Pay attention to the two types of inability mentioned.
2
Identify the two types of inability
Al-Nasafi distinguishes between inability due to lack of means/instruments and inability due to lack of real power (qudra). Find where he makes this distinction.
The first type is not blameworthy; the second is.
3
Analyze the blame argument
Understand why blame only applies to the absence of real power when means are present. Al-Nasafi argues that if means were missing, the person would be compelled and not blamed.
Blame requires free choice and capacity.
4
Consider the supporting verse
Reflect on the second Quranic example from Moses and Khidr (18:72), which reinforces that real inability (to have patience) is distinct from lacking means.
This verse confirms that real power is a distinct entity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما دليل ثبوت الاستطاعة التي هي حقيقة القدرة فقوله تعالى: ﴿ مَا كَانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ ﴾ والمراد منه نفي حقيقة القدرة لا نفي الأسباب والآلات؛ لأنها كانت ثابتة، وإنما المنتفى عنهم كان حقيقة القدرة التي بها يتعلق الفعل. يحققه أنه ذكر ذلك على وجه الذم لهم، والذم إنما يلحقهم بانعدام حقيقة القدرة عند وجود الأسباب وصحة الآلات لا بانعدام سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات، لأن انتفاء تلك الاستطاعة لم تكن بتضييعه بل هو في ذلك مجبور، وأما انتفاء حقيقة القدرة فموجب ذمهم؛ لأن انعدامها مع سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات كانت بتضييعه إياها لاشتغاله بضد ما أمر به. يحققه أنه خص بنفس هذه الاستطاعة الكافر، وانتفاء تلك الاستطاعة يستوي فيه المسلم والكافر، وإنما المختص بالكافر هو انتفاء هذه الاستطاعة، والدليل عليه قول صاحب موسى لموسى عليهما السلام : ﴿ إِنَّكَ لَن تَسْتَطِيعَ مَعِيَ صَبْرًا ﴾
As for the evidence for the affirmation of the ability which is the true power (haqiqat al-qudra), it is His statement, the Exalted: 'They were not able to hear' (Quran 11:20). What is intended by it is the negation of true power, not the negation of means and instruments, because they were present. Rather, what was negated from them was the true power by which the act is connected. He confirms that He mentioned it as a blame upon them, and blame only attaches to them due to the absence of true power when means are present and instruments are sound, not due to the absence of soundness of means and health of instruments, because the absence of that ability (i.e., of means) was not due to their own neglect, but they were compelled in that. As for the absence of true power, it necessitates blame upon them, because its absence with sound means and healthy instruments was due to their own neglect, because they busied themselves with the opposite of what they were commanded. He confirms that the disbeliever is specifically characterized by this very ability, while the absence of that ability (i.e., of means) is shared by Muslim and disbeliever alike. What is specific to the disbeliever is the absence of this ability. The evidence for it is the statement of the companion of Moses to Moses, peace be upon them: 'Indeed, you will never be able to have patience with me' (Quran 18:72).
Source pages p. 788

Commentary
This passage is a proof-text argument for the existence of the second type of istita'a, which is true power (haqiqat al-qudra). The author cites Quran 11:20, which says of the disbelievers 'they were not able to hear.' He argues that this negation cannot be of means and instruments because those were present; rather it is a negation of real power (qudra) by which acts are performed. The verse is stated as a blame, and blame only applies when real power is absent despite sound means. If real power were absent due to lack of means, the person would be compelled and not blameworthy. But the disbelievers' inability to hear is blameworthy because they had the means but lacked real power due to their own fault—they busied themselves with opposition to what they were commanded. The author then confirms that this real power is specifically negated from disbelievers; the inability due to lack of means is common to both Muslims and disbelievers. He supports this with the story of Moses and Khidr (Quran 18:72), where Khidr tells Moses 'you will never be able to have patience with me'—this is a real inability (lack of capacity for patience), not a lack of means. Thus, the passage establishes a distinct type of istita'a which is real power, and its absence is blameworthy when one has the means.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that inability due to lack of means is blameworthy.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that only inability due to lack of real power (qudra) is blameworthy; inability due to lack of means is not, because the person is compelled.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, why are disbelievers blamed in Quran 11:20 for not being able to hear?

B) Because they had healthy organs but lacked real power due to their own fault
C) Because they were physically deaf
D) Because Allah did not create hearing for them

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi proves that real power is a distinct type of ability, and its absence is blameworthy when means are present, as shown in Quran 11:20 and 18:72.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fall short in your duties to Allah, do you find yourself blaming your circumstances (lack of time, resources, health) rather than your own lack of real resolve? Where in your life is your 'inability' actually a cover for neglected responsibility?
?
The disbelievers are blamed because they busied themselves with the opposite of what they were commanded. In what specific area of your life are you currently busying yourself with the opposite of Allah's command, while excusing yourself as 'unable' to change?
?
You likely have sound means—health, intellect, wealth—yet you still fail. What if your failure is not due to missing means but to a missing real power that you yourself have squandered? Will you continue to excuse yourself, or will you beg Allah for true ability?

Proof that Capacity is an Accident and Refutation of Dissenters
Proves istita'a is an accident and refutes dissenters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that human capacity (istita'a) is an accident distinct from the body, and how this proof invalidates three major sectarian positions that deny, reduce, or misidentify capacity.

Core Idea
Capacity is an added accident, proven by observable variation in human ability.

This passage from Tabshirat al-Adilla presents a key argument in the Maturidi refutation of Mu'tazilite and other views on human capacity. Imam al-Nasafi first establishes that capacity (istita'a) is an accident (arad) beyond the body, using a simple empirical observation and an analogy. He then applies this conclusion to reject the claims of Nazzam, Ghaylan, Dirar, and others, showing that the correct understanding of capacity is essential for sound theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold: he first states what is refuted, then gives the proof, then applies it.
2
Understand the analogy of twisted threads
The analogy compares capacity to twisting in threads: just as twisting (an accident) increases resistance without adding substance, capacity increases ability without changing the limbs. This is key to seeing capacity as an accident.
3
See how each refuted group's error is uncovered
Identify the three groups: those who deny capacity entirely (Nazzam), those who reduce it to bodily health (Ghaylan et al.), and those who make it part of the body (Dirar). Note how the single proof refutes all three.
Each error is a different corruption of the concept of capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطل بهذا قول من يقول: لا استطاعة للإنسان إذ هي ليست معنى وراء المستطيع بل الإنسان مستطيع بنفسه لا باستطاعة كما ذهب إليه النظام وعلى الأسواري وأبو بكر الأصم. الاستطاعة عرض وراء الذات لأنا بينا بالدليل ثبوتها وهي عرض من الأعراض، ولا شك أن العرض معنى وراء الجسم، والذي يدل على ثبوتها أنا وجدنا الإنسان سليم الجوارح ليس بذي آفة وهو قادر على حمل خمسين رطلاً، ثم وجدناه في حالة أخرى قادرا على حمل مائة رطل من غير زيادة في أجزاء أعضائه، ونظيره خيطان منشوران يصعب قطعهما، وإذا فتلا يصعب القطع من غير زيادة في أجزاء الخيطين بل لحدوث الفتل وهو عرض في نفسه. وبهذا يبطل أيضًا قول غيلان وأتباعه وثمامة بن الأشرس وبشر بن المعتمر: أن الاستطاعة ليست غير سلامة الأسباب وصحة الجوارح وتخليها عن الآفات. وبهذا أيضًا يبطل قول ضرار وحفص الفرد أنها بعض المستطيع لما ثبت أنها عرض، والقول بكون العرض بعض الجسم محال. والله الموفق.
And by this is refuted the saying of those who say: There is no capacity for man, for it is not a meaning beyond the capable, rather man is capable by himself not by a capacity, as al-Nazzam, Ali al-Uswari, and Abu Bakr al-Asamm held. Capacity is an accident beyond the essence, for we have proven by evidence its existence, and it is an accident among accidents, and there is no doubt that the accident is a meaning beyond the body. And what indicates its existence is that we find a man with sound limbs, free from defect, able to carry fifty ratls, then we find him in another state able to carry one hundred ratls without any increase in the parts of his limbs. And its analogy is two spread-out threads which are difficult to cut, and when twisted, cutting becomes difficult without any increase in the parts of the two threads, but due to the occurrence of twisting, which is an accident in itself. And by this is also refuted the saying of Ghaylan and his followers, Thumama ibn al-Ashras, and Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir: that capacity is nothing but soundness of means, health of limbs, and their being free from defects. And by this also is refuted the saying of Dirar and Hafs al-Fard that it is part of the capable, because it has been established that it is an accident, and the statement that an accident is part of a body is impossible. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 789

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part refutation of several erroneous views regarding human capacity (al-istita'a). The author first establishes that capacity is an accident (arad) distinct from the body, then uses this to refute three groups. The proof for capacity being an accident is based on observable variation: a man with the same limbs can carry different weights (50 vs 100 ratls), indicating an additional attribute (capacity) that increases. The analogy of twisted threads shows that twisting (an accident) makes cutting harder without increasing the threads' substance. Thus, capacity is a real meaning beyond the body. This refutes the Nazzamiyya who deny capacity as a distinct meaning. Second, it refutes Ghaylan, Thumama, and Bishr who equate capacity with merely sound limbs and absence of defects. Third, it refutes Dirar and Hafs who claim capacity is part of the capable person, because an accident cannot be a part of a body.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة
العرض
النظام
غيلان
ضرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Capacity is nothing but soundness of limbs and absence of defects (the view of Ghaylan et al.).
Correction: The proof shows capacity is an additional accident beyond bodily health, as evidenced by variation in ability without change in limbs.

Checkpoint
What is the main proof that capacity (al-istita'a) is an accident beyond the body?

D) A hadith from the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The observable variation in human ability proves that capacity is a real accident beyond the body, refuting those who deny or misdefine it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

First Capacity: Preceding the Act and Suitability for Opposites
Describes the first capacity: precedes act and is suitable for opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two key characteristics of the first capacity: that it precedes the act and that it is neutral, suitable for both good and evil actions.

Core Idea
The first capacity is a neutral precondition for action, not a determinant of good or evil.

In this passage, the author explains the nature of the first capacity (al-istita'a al-ula). He draws on consensus among those who affirm human capacity and actions to establish that this capacity precedes the act. Furthermore, he illustrates that this capacity is equally suited for opposite actions, making it morally neutral. As you read, pay attention to how the examples reinforce the idea that the capacity itself does not necessitate a particular outcome.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic carefully. Notice the structure: first a general statement of consensus, then examples, then the key point about opposites.
2
Identify the two characteristics
Find where the author states that the first capacity precedes the act, and then where he says it is suitable for opposites. Write them down.
The examples help clarify each characteristic.
3
Reflect on the moral neutrality
Consider the implications: the same hand can be used for jihad or for fighting Muslims. What does this tell you about the role of human capacity in determining good and evil actions?
This ties to broader discussions in kalam about human agency and divine decree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أجمع القائلون بالاستطاعة المثبتون للعبد الأعمال أن الاستطاعة الأولى تتقدم الفعل، فإن اليد السليمة والرجل الصحيحة يتقدمان البطش والمشي، والزاد والراحلة يتقدمان وجود أفعال الحج، وكذلك يصلح للضدين، فإن اليد الصحيحة كما تصلح لجهاد الكفار تصلح لقتال أهل الإسلام، وكذا الرجل السليمة كما تصلح للمشي إلى المساجد تصلح للمشي إلى بيوت الخمارين والزواني.
Then those who affirm capacity and affirm actions for the slave are in agreement that the first capacity precedes the act. For the sound hand and healthy foot precede striking and walking, and provisions and the mount precede the existence of the actions of Hajj. And likewise it is suitable for opposites: the sound hand, just as it is suitable for fighting disbelievers, it is suitable for fighting Muslims; and similarly the healthy foot, just as it is suitable for walking to mosques, it is suitable for walking to houses of drunkards and adulteresses.
Source pages p. 789

Commentary
This passage defines the first capacity (al-istita'a al-ula). It is a classification passage: the author states that all who affirm capacity and human actions agree that the first capacity precedes the act. He gives examples: the sound hand and foot exist before the actions of striking and walking; provisions and mount exist before Hajj actions. Then he notes that this first capacity is suitable for opposites (salih li-diddain): the same hand can be used for good (jihad) or evil (fighting Muslims); the same foot can go to mosque or to sinful places. This shows that the first capacity is neutral and does not determine the act.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة الأولى
الضدان
تقدم الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The first capacity necessarily leads to a specific action.
Correction: The first capacity is merely preparatory and neutral; it can be used for either good or evil actions, as shown by the examples.

Checkpoint

A) It is simultaneous with the act.
B) It follows the act.
C) It precedes the act and is suitable for opposites.
D) It is identical to the act.

Key Takeaway
The first capacity is a neutral precondition that precedes the act and is equally suitable for good or evil actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Your feet carry you to places every day. List one good place you went this week and one sinful place (even mentally). Did you reflect before walking? How will you remind yourself tomorrow that your capacity is neutral and you are responsible for directing it?
?
This lesson strips away the excuse 'I couldn't help it because I have this ability.' When you sinned, did you ever blame your capacity? Now that you know the first capacity is neutral, whose fault is it? What will you actually change about your choices today?

The Timing of the Second Capacity: Preceding or Concurrent?
Presents two opposing views on whether the second capacity precedes or accompanies the act, with a rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two major positions on whether the second capacity (al-istita'ah al-thaniyah) precedes or accompanies the act, and the rational proof for concurrence based on the nature of accidents.

Core Idea
The second capacity is an accident; since accidents cannot endure, it must coexist with the act.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents a key debate within Islamic theology about the timing of the capacity that directly enables actions. The Mu'tazila and others argued that this capacity must precede the act, while the Maturid school, along with Ahl al-Hadith and the Najjariyya, insisted it must be concurrent. The decisive proof rests on the nature of accidents. Let's examine the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two views
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the two opposing positions: precedence vs. concurrence.
The passage starts by stating the disagreement.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila and Dirariyya (and most Karramiyya) claim the second capacity precedes the act and that concurrence is impossible.
They see capacity as a prerequisite that must be in place before the act.
3
Examine the Maturidi proof
Our school and others argue for concurrence because capacity is an originated accident, and accidents cannot endure. If it preceded, it would vanish before the act, leaving no capacity at the moment of action.
This is a rational argument based on the nature of accidents.
4
Reflect on the theological stakes
Without concurrent capacity, actions would occur without divine or human power, which is impossible. This shows why concurrence is necessary.
The proof ties capacity to actual agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الاستطاعة الثانية فقد اختلفوا في جواز تقدمها على الفعل، فزعمت المعتزلة والضرارية : أنها تكون سابقة على الفعل ويستحيل اقترانها به، وإليه ذهب أكثر الكرامية. وقال أصحابنا وجميع متكلمي أهل الحديث والنجارية: إنها تكون مع الفعل ومحال تقدمها على الفعل. وذلك لأن القدرة الحادثة عرض، والعرض يستحيل بقاؤه، فلو كانت القدرة سابقة على الفعل لانعدمت وقت الفعل فيكون فعل بدون قدرة وهذا مستحيل لأنه يترتب عليه وجود العالم بدون قدرة الله ووجود عمل للإنسان بدون استطاعته.
As for the second capacity, they differed regarding the permissibility of its preceding the act. So the Mu'tazila and Dirariyya claimed that it precedes the act and that its being concurrent with it is impossible; and most of the Karramiyya held this view. And our companions (Ashabuna) and all the mutakallimun of the Ahl al-Hadith and the Najjariyya said: it is concurrent with the act and its preceding the act is impossible. That is because the originated capacity is an accident, and the accident is impossible to subsist. So if capacity preceded the act, it would cease to exist at the time of the act, resulting in an act without capacity, and this is impossible because it would entail the existence of the world without God's capacity and the existence of an action for man without his capacity.
Source pages p. 790

Commentary
This passage presents a theological disagreement about the second capacity (al-istita'a al-thaniya), which is the capacity that directly enables the act. The author contrasts two positions: the Mu'tazila and Dirariyya, along with most Karramiyya, hold that this capacity must precede the act and cannot coexist with it. The opposing view, held by the author's school (Maturidis), the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith, and the Najjariyya, is that the second capacity is concurrent with the act and cannot precede it. The proof given is that the originated capacity (al-qudra al-haditha) is an accident, and accidents cannot endure (baqa'). If it preceded the act, it would vanish by the time of the act, leaving the act without capacity, which is impossible because it would imply creation without divine power and human action without capacity. Thus, the capacity must be present simultaneously with the act.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة الثانية
القدرة الحادثة
اقتران
بقاء العرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think capacity must always precede the act, in the sense that one must have the ability before acting.
Correction: For the second capacity (the capacity directly enabling the act), it must be concurrent because as an accident it cannot endure; if it preceded, it would vanish at the moment of action.

Checkpoint
Why do the Maturidis and others hold that the second capacity cannot precede the act?
A) Because the act would then be prior to capacity.
B) Because capacity is an accident and cannot endure, so it would vanish if before the act.
C) Because the Quran explicitly states it.
D) Because the first capacity already suffices.

Key Takeaway
The second capacity must be concurrent with the act because as an accident it cannot endure, making precedence impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an action, do you truly believe that your capacity to do it is given to you at that very moment by Allah, not something you stored up from before? How would this change your reliance on Him right before you act?
?
What would it mean for your sense of control if you accepted that the ability to act cannot exist even a second before the act itself? Does that thought unsettle you, or does it bring you closer to recognizing Allah's constant involvement?
?
The passage argues that an accident cannot endure; your capacity is an accident. Can you point to one area of your life where you've assumed your ability is self-sustaining, and ask yourself: 'Am I really acting with a capacity that I own, or am I borrowing it moment by moment from Allah?'

The Power Cannot Be Attached to the Existent
First argument: power cannot attach to the existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first argument: the power of bringing into existence cannot be attached to an already existing act.

Core Idea
Power over the existent is impossible; it must be over the non-existent.

Nasafi begins his refutation of the Mu'tazilite position by examining the very nature of power. The first argument targets the claim that ability (qudra) can precede the act. He argues that if power is meant to bring something into existence, it can only be attached to what is not yet existent. This lesson walks through that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument's premise
The argument begins: power cannot be attached to the existent because bringing the existent into existence is impossible. Understand why this is a foundational point.
The key word is 'إيجاد الموجود'—bringing the existent into existence, which is a contradiction.
2
Follow the conditional implication
If power precedes the act, it must be over the non-existent. But if it is simultaneous with the act, it would be attached to the existent—which is impossible. So power cannot precede the act.
Nasafi uses a conditional to show the absurdity of the Mu'tazilite position.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Conclude that the Mu'tazilite claim that ability exists before the act is logically impossible, because it would require power over an already existing thing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن قدرة الإيجاد يستحيل تعلقها بالموجود لما في إيجاد الموجود من الاستحالة فإذا هي تتعلق بالمعدوم ليوجد بها، وإنما تكون قدرة على المعدوم دون الموجود أن لو كانت سابقة عليه، فأما إذا كانت مقارنة للفعل فهي متعلقة بالموجود، وهو محال، ولأن القدرة لو كانت الفعل لم تكن القدرة بكونها علة لوجود الفعل أولى من القلب إذ خروجها من العدم إلى الوجود مطابقا فلا يمكن إضافة وجود أحدهما إلى الآخر بل أضيف وجودهما جميعًا إلى غيرهما، ولو أضيف وجود الفعل إلى القدرة مع استواء حالهما لجاز إضافة وجود القدرة إلى الفعل، ولأنه لو كان لا يؤمن حتى يقدر ولا يقدر حتى يؤمن يبقى أبدًا غير مؤمن كالواقع في البشر إذا كان لا يخرج حتى يأتيه بالحبل ولا يأتيه بالحبل حتى يخرج لم يخرج أبدًا، ولأن الكافر لو لم يكن معه قدرة الإيمان لكان معذورًا ولم يكن تعذيبه عدلاً، إذ لا عذر للعبد في الشاهد أعظم من أن يقول: لو قيل له لم لم تفعل كذا؟ فيقول : لأني لم أقدر عليه، فمثله في الغائب، ويسألون ويقولون هل اتقى أحد معصية الله تعالى وهو قادر عليها مراقبة الله تعالى؟ فإن قلتم : لا، فقد أعظمتم القول في وصف الأنبياء عليهم السلام، وينبغي أن لا يثاب في الاتقاء عن المعاصي وإن قلتم : نعم، فقد أقررتم بوجود الاستطاعة ولا فعل.
And because the power of bringing into existence cannot possibly be attached to the existent due to the impossibility in bringing the existent into existence, so it is attached to the non-existent to be brought into existence by it. And it would be a power over the non-existent without the existent if it had preceded it. But if it is concomitant with the act, then it is attached to the existent, and that is impossible. And because if power were the act, power would not be more deserving to be a cause for the existence of the act than the reverse (al-qalb), since their emergence from non-existence to existence is matching; so it is not possible to attribute the existence of one to the other, rather the existence of both is attributed to something else. And if the existence of the act were attributed to power while their state is equal, it would be permissible to attribute the existence of power to the act. And because if he would not believe until he is able and would not be able until he believes, he would remain forever a non-believer, like someone stuck in a well if he does not come out until he brings a rope and does not bring a rope until he comes out, he never comes out. And because if the disbeliever did not possess the power of faith, he would be excused and his punishment would not be just. For in the perceptible world, there is no greater excuse for a servant than if it is said to him: 'Why did you not do such-and-such?' and he says: 'Because I was not capable of it.' The same applies in the unseen. They ask and say: 'Did anyone avoid a disobedience of God while being capable of it, fearing God?' If you say: 'No', then you have committed a grave statement regarding the description of the prophets (peace be upon them), and it would mean that one should not be rewarded for avoiding sins. And if you say: 'Yes', then you have admitted the existence of ability without act.
Source pages p. 793

Commentary
This passage is a series of four arguments refuting the Mu'tazilite claim that ability (al-istita'a) exists before the act. The author presents them as refutations of their position. 

First argument: The power of bringing into existence (qudrat al-ijad) cannot be attached to an existent thing because bringing the existent into existence is impossible. It must be attached to the non-existent. If it were to precede the act, it would be a power over the non-existent, but if it is simultaneous with the act, it would be attached to the existent—which is impossible. Thus, the power cannot precede the act. 

Second argument: If power were the act, it would not be more appropriate to be the cause of the act than the reverse, because both emerge from non-existence to existence equally. Therefore, the existence of neither can be attributed to the other; rather both are from God. If one were attributed to the other, one could equally attribute power's existence to the act. 

Third argument: If a person cannot believe until he has the ability, and cannot have the ability until he believes, he would remain forever in a state of disbelief—like a person trapped in a well who can only get out by bringing a rope but cannot bring a rope until he gets out. This is a vicious circle that leads to impossibility. 

Fourth argument: If the disbeliever had no ability to believe, he would be excused and punishment would be unjust. In human experience, the greatest excuse is lack of ability. The same applies in the unseen. Moreover, if one denies that anyone can avoid sin while being able, that would impugn the prophets, and it would mean no reward for avoiding sin. If one affirms it, then one admits ability exists even when not used—which contradicts the Mu'tazilite claim that ability only exists with the act.

Key Terms
قدرة
إيجاد
موجود
معدوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason given that power cannot be attached to the existent?
A) Because the existent is already perfect.
B) Because bringing the existent into existence is impossible.
C) Because power is a substance.
D) Because the existent is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The first argument shows that power can only be over the non-existent, so it cannot accompany the act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever attribute the power to bring something into existence to your own ability, forgetting that only Allah creates? Reflect on a time you felt you were the sole cause of a success. How does this argument redirect your gratitude?
?
If your power to act can only exist before the act, not during it, then what does that imply about your actual role in each moment of your life? Are you truly in control, or are you constantly receiving power from Allah?
?
The argument shows that attaching power to an already existing thing is impossible. Yet we often try to 'change' what already is by our own effort. What is one situation in your life where you are trying to exert power over something that already exists (e.g., regret, a fixed circumstance)? How can you let go and trust Allah's decree instead?

Power as Cause: Symmetry Argument
Second argument: power cannot cause the act due to symmetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument: if power were the cause of the act, there would be no reason to prefer it over the reverse, so both must come from God.

Core Idea
Power and act emerge equally from non-existence, so neither can cause the other.

The second argument targets the causal relationship between power and the act. Nasafi argues that if power were the cause of the act, then by the same logic the act could be the cause of power, leading to absurdity. This lesson explores the principle of 'qalb' (reversal).

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise of equal emergence
Both power and act come into existence from non-existence in a matching way. There is no inherent priority.
The phrase 'مطابقا' indicates their emergence is symmetrical.
2
Apply the principle of reversal (qalb)
If one is the cause of the other, then by symmetry the reverse is equally valid. That would allow attributing the existence of power to the act.
This leads to an unacceptable circular causality.
3
Conclude both from another source
Since neither can be the cause of the other, both must be caused by something else—namely, God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?
The argument shows that attributing your power as the cause of your action is logically absurd. Yet you live as if your power is the cause. What specific situation today will you remind yourself that your power is merely a created thing, not the creator of your actions?
?

The Vicious Circle of Ability and Belief
Third argument: circularity leads to impossibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third argument: the Mu'tazilite claim leads to a vicious circle that makes belief impossible.

Core Idea
If ability requires belief and belief requires ability, neither ever occurs.

The third argument is a classic reductio ad absurdum: if a person cannot believe until he has the ability to believe, and cannot have the ability until he believes, then he will never believe. Nasafi illustrates this with a powerful analogy of a man trapped in a well. This lesson examines the logical structure of circularity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional cycle
The argument states: 'he would not believe until he is able, and would not be able until he believes.' This creates a mutual dependency.
The phrase 'لو كان لا يؤمن حتى يقدر ولا يقدر حتى يؤمن' sets up the cycle.
2
Analyze the well analogy
Like a man in a well who cannot get out without a rope and cannot get the rope without getting out, the cycle ensures he never gets out.
The analogy makes the impossibility intuitive.
3
Conclude the impossibility
Therefore, the Mu'tazilite position that ability must exist before the act (here, belief) leads to the absurd conclusion that belief is never attained.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن قدرة الإيجاد يستحيل تعلقها بالموجود لما في إيجاد الموجود من الاستحالة فإذا هي تتعلق بالمعدوم ليوجد بها، وإنما تكون قدرة على المعدوم دون الموجود أن لو كانت سابقة عليه، فأما إذا كانت مقارنة للفعل فهي متعلقة بالموجود، وهو محال، ولأن القدرة لو كانت الفعل لم تكن القدرة بكونها علة لوجود الفعل أولى من القلب إذ خروجها من العدم إلى الوجود مطابقا فلا يمكن إضافة وجود أحدهما إلى الآخر بل أضيف وجودهما جميعًا إلى غيرهما، ولو أضيف وجود الفعل إلى القدرة مع استواء حالهما لجاز إضافة وجود القدرة إلى الفعل، ولأنه لو كان لا يؤمن حتى يقدر ولا يقدر حتى يؤمن يبقى أبدًا غير مؤمن كالواقع في البشر إذا كان لا يخرج حتى يأتيه بالحبل ولا يأتيه بالحبل حتى يخرج لم يخرج أبدًا، ولأن الكافر لو لم يكن معه قدرة الإيمان لكان معذورًا ولم يكن تعذيبه عدلاً، إذ لا عذر للعبد في الشاهد أعظم من أن يقول: لو قيل له لم لم تفعل كذا؟ فيقول : لأني لم أقدر عليه، فمثله في الغائب، ويسألون ويقولون هل اتقى أحد معصية الله تعالى وهو قادر عليها مراقبة الله تعالى؟ فإن قلتم : لا، فقد أعظمتم القول في وصف الأنبياء عليهم السلام، وينبغي أن لا يثاب في الاتقاء عن المعاصي وإن قلتم : نعم، فقد أقررتم بوجود الاستطاعة ولا فعل.

?

?

?

The Excuse Argument and the Existence of Ability Without Act
Fourth argument: no ability would excuse disbeliever, and ability exists without act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth argument: that denying ability to the disbeliever would excuse him unjustly, and that ability exists even when not used.

Core Idea
If the disbeliever had no ability, he would be excused, contradicting divine justice.

The fourth argument combines two points: first, if the disbeliever lacked the ability to believe, he would have a valid excuse for disbelief, making punishment unjust. Second, the Mu'tazilite claim that ability only exists with the act is refuted by the fact that righteous people avoid sins while being able to commit them—showing ability without act.

Guided Path
1
Understand the excuse premise
If a disbeliever has no ability to believe, he can say 'I was not capable,' which is the greatest excuse in human experience.
This directly challenges the justice of eternal punishment.
2
Apply the same logic to the unseen
The excuse of incapacity is universal, so God would be unjust to punish the disbeliever if he truly lacked ability.
3
Consider the avoidance of sin by the pious
If one denies that anyone can avoid sin while being able, that would impugn the prophets. If one affirms it, then ability exists without the act of sinning.
This proves that ability can be present even when not used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن قدرة الإيجاد يستحيل تعلقها بالموجود لما في إيجاد الموجود من الاستحالة فإذا هي تتعلق بالمعدوم ليوجد بها، وإنما تكون قدرة على المعدوم دون الموجود أن لو كانت سابقة عليه، فأما إذا كانت مقارنة للفعل فهي متعلقة بالموجود، وهو محال، ولأن القدرة لو كانت الفعل لم تكن القدرة بكونها علة لوجود الفعل أولى من القلب إذ خروجها من العدم إلى الوجود مطابقا فلا يمكن إضافة وجود أحدهما إلى الآخر بل أضيف وجودهما جميعًا إلى غيرهما، ولو أضيف وجود الفعل إلى القدرة مع استواء حالهما لجاز إضافة وجود القدرة إلى الفعل، ولأنه لو كان لا يؤمن حتى يقدر ولا يقدر حتى يؤمن يبقى أبدًا غير مؤمن كالواقع في البشر إذا كان لا يخرج حتى يأتيه بالحبل ولا يأتيه بالحبل حتى يخرج لم يخرج أبدًا، ولأن الكافر لو لم يكن معه قدرة الإيمان لكان معذورًا ولم يكن تعذيبه عدلاً، إذ لا عذر للعبد في الشاهد أعظم من أن يقول: لو قيل له لم لم تفعل كذا؟ فيقول : لأني لم أقدر عليه، فمثله في الغائب، ويسألون ويقولون هل اتقى أحد معصية الله تعالى وهو قادر عليها مراقبة الله تعالى؟ فإن قلتم : لا، فقد أعظمتم القول في وصف الأنبياء عليهم السلام، وينبغي أن لا يثاب في الاتقاء عن المعاصي وإن قلتم : نعم، فقد أقررتم بوجود الاستطاعة ولا فعل.
And because the power of bringing into existence cannot possibly be attached to the existent due to the impossibility in bringing the existent into existence, so it is attached to the non-existent to be brought into existence by it. And it would be a power over the non-existent without the existent if it had preceded it. But if it is concomitant with the act, then it is attached to the existent, and that is impossible. And because if power were the act, power would not be more deserving to be a cause for the existence of the act than the reverse (al-qalb), since their emergence from non-existence to existence is matching; so it is not possible to attribute the existence of one to the other, rather the existence of both is attributed to something else. And if the existence of the act were attributed to power while their state is equal, it would be permissible to attribute the existence of power to the act. And because if he would not believe until he is able and would not be able until he believes, he would remain forever a non-believer, like someone stuck in a well if he does not come out until he brings a rope and does not bring a rope until he comes out, he never comes out. And because if the disbeliever did not possess the power of faith, he would be excused and his punishment would not be just. For in the perceptible world, there is no greater excuse for a servant than if it is said to him: 'Why did you not do such-and-such?' and he says: 'Because I was not capable of it.' The same applies in the unseen. They ask and say: 'Did anyone avoid a disobedience of God while being capable of it, fearing God?' If you say: 'No', then you have committed a grave statement regarding the description of the prophets (peace be upon them), and it would mean that one should not be rewarded for avoiding sins. And if you say: 'Yes', then you have admitted the existence of ability without act.
Source pages p. 793

Commentary
This passage is a series of four arguments refuting the Mu'tazilite claim that ability (al-istita'a) exists before the act. The author presents them as refutations of their position. 

First argument: The power of bringing into existence (qudrat al-ijad) cannot be attached to an existent thing because bringing the existent into existence is impossible. It must be attached to the non-existent. If it were to precede the act, it would be a power over the non-existent, but if it is simultaneous with the act, it would be attached to the existent—which is impossible. Thus, the power cannot precede the act. 

Second argument: If power were the act, it would not be more appropriate to be the cause of the act than the reverse, because both emerge from non-existence to existence equally. Therefore, the existence of neither can be attributed to the other; rather both are from God. If one were attributed to the other, one could equally attribute power's existence to the act. 

Third argument: If a person cannot believe until he has the ability, and cannot have the ability until he believes, he would remain forever in a state of disbelief—like a person trapped in a well who can only get out by bringing a rope but cannot bring a rope until he gets out. This is a vicious circle that leads to impossibility. 

Fourth argument: If the disbeliever had no ability to believe, he would be excused and punishment would be unjust. In human experience, the greatest excuse is lack of ability. The same applies in the unseen. Moreover, if one denies that anyone can avoid sin while being able, that would impugn the prophets, and it would mean no reward for avoiding sin. If one affirms it, then one admits ability exists even when not used—which contradicts the Mu'tazilite claim that ability only exists with the act.

Key Terms
كافر
قدرة
عذر
اتقاء
معصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite claim that ability only exists with the act (i.e., at the moment of action).
Correction: The righteous avoid sins while being capable, proving ability can exist without the act.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth argument, what is the consequence if the disbeliever had no ability?
A) He would still be punished justly.
B) He would be excused and punishment would be unjust.
C) He would have no excuse.
D) He would not exist.

Key Takeaway
The fourth argument shows that denying ability leads to unjust punishment and that ability exists without act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument shows that the disbeliever had the ability to believe but chose disbelief. In your own life, where have you used the excuse 'I couldn't' to avoid an Islamic obligation when in reality you had the ability? Will you stop using that excuse starting today?
?
Consider a sin you committed while being fully capable of avoiding it. How does the fact that the righteous avoid sins while capable challenge your own accountability? What one practical step will you take this week to strengthen your self-control and fear of God?
?
The passage says there is no greater excuse than 'I was not capable.' Is there any area of your faith—prayer, charity, patience—where you have hidden behind that excuse? What would it cost you to admit you had the ability all along?

The Simultaneity of Power and Act
Al-Nasafi argues that qudra must accompany the act, not precede it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Nasafi argues that human power (qudra) must accompany the act and cannot precede it, and how his reasoning exposes a logical contradiction if it were otherwise.

Core Idea
Power cannot precede the act without causing logical chaos.

This passage presents a concise but powerful argument for a key Maturidi position on qadar. Al-Nasafi begins by stating his thesis, then deploys a reductio: if power preceded the act without persisting, the act would exist without power, leading to contradictions in the definitions of power and incapacity. By working through this argument, you will see how the simultaneity of power and act is rationally necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Note the key terms: الاستطاعة, القدرة, العجز.
2
Identify the thesis and its premises
The passage opens with a clear thesis: capacity is an accident that occurs with the act. Then al-Nasafi introduces a crucial premise: power does not persist over time. Find these statements.
The premise about non-persistence is agreed upon by many Mu'tazila.
3
Follow the reductio argument
Trace the hypothetical: 'if power preceded and had no survival.' What follows? The act would exist without power, and power would only cease to its opposite (incapacity). This leads to the agent being both powerful and incapable – a contradiction.
The author uses a form of argument known as 'reductio ad absurdum'.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The argument concludes that power must be simultaneous with the act. If not, the definitions of power and incapacity would swap. Consider why this is a necessary conclusion for the Maturidi school.
This is a foundational point in Maturidi theology about human agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاستطاعة عرض يكون مع الفعل. إن القدرة لما كانت غير قابلة للبقاء، وساعدنا عليه كثير من المعتزلة، وأثبتنا ذلك بالدليل على من أبي القول، ولو كانت هي متقدمة على الفعل ولا بقاء إلى الثاني من الأوقات كانت عدمًا وقت وجود الفعل، فيوجد الفعل ولا قدرة، وهي لا تنعدم عمن يجوز قيامها به إلا عما يضادها وهو العجز، ومن انعدمت قدرته يستحيل اتصافه بكونه قادرًا، ومن قام به العجز يستحيل أن لا يكون عاجزا، فعلى هذا التقدير يكون الفعل مستحيل الوجود من القادر واجب الوجود من العاجز، ومن هذا قوله، فهو قد أصيب بعقله ولم يشعر. يحققه أن الفعل لو جاز وجوده مع انعدام القدرة بل وجب وهي لا تنعدم إلا إلى عجز، واستحال وجوده مع وجودها لكانت القدرة هي العجز والعجز هو القدرة، فإنا لا نعرف العجز إلا بأن يستحيل معه الفعل والقدرة إلا بأن يجب بها الفعل ويثبت.
Capacity (al-istita'a) is an accident that occurs with the act. Indeed, since power (al-qudra) is not susceptible to remaining, and many of the Mu'tazila agreed with us on that, and we established that by evidence against those who refused the statement, had it preceded the act and had no survival to the second moment, it would be nonexistent at the time of the act's existence; so the act exists and there is no power. And it (power) does not cease from the one in whom its subsistence is possible except by what opposes it, which is incapacity (al-‘ajz). Whoever's power ceases, it is impossible for him to be described as powerful. Whoever is characterized by incapacity, it is impossible for him not to be incapable. According to this estimation, the act would be impossible from the powerful and necessary from the incapable. From this is his statement – he has been struck in his mind and did not realize. What verifies this is that if the act's existence were possible with the absence of power, but rather necessary – and it (power) does not cease except to incapacity – and its existence with its presence is impossible, then power would be incapacity and incapacity would be power. For we do not know incapacity except by the act being impossible with it, and power except by the act being necessarily effected by it and established.
Source pages p. 809

Commentary
This passage is a proof that human power (qudra) must accompany the act, not precede it. The author begins by stating the thesis: capacity (istita'a) is an accident (‛arad) that occurs simultaneously with the act. He then argues that power cannot persist over time (it is not qābil li-l-baqā'), a point agreed upon by many Mu‘tazila. Had power preceded the act without surviving to the next moment, it would be absent exactly when the act occurs. This leads to absurdity: the act would exist without a power, and power only ceases due to its opposite, incapacity (‛ajz). The agent would then be both powerful (when power existed) and incapable (when it ceases), resulting in the act being impossible from the powerful and necessary from the incapable – a contradiction. The author reinforces this by noting that if the act occurred without power while being impossible with it, the definitions of power and incapacity would be swapped. Thus, power must be simultaneous with the act.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة (capacity)
القدرة (power)
العجز (incapacity)
العرض (accident)
الفعل (act)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that human power (qudra) exists independently before the act, like a stored ability.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that if power preceded without persisting, the act would occur without power, leading to logical chaos. Power must be simultaneous with the act for coherent agency.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what would happen if power (qudra) preceded the act and did not survive to the next moment?
A) The act would occur with power present.
B) The act would occur without power, making the act necessary from the incapable.
C) Power would remain forever.
D) The act would be impossible from both the powerful and the incapable.

Key Takeaway
Power must be simultaneous with the act; otherwise, the act would be impossible from the powerful and necessary from the incapable, which is absurd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you attribute your every successful action to Allah's creation of power within you at that very moment, or do you subconsciously think you have an independent store of power? How would your gratitude change if you truly internalized that your capacity to act is given anew each instant?
?
Consider a moment when you failed to do something good. Did you feel that your power had simply 'run out'? According to al-Nasafi's argument, incapacity only arises from the opposite of power. What does your failure reveal about the state of your reliance on Allah?
?
The passage shows that assuming power precedes the act leads to absurdity. In your daily life, where might you be assuming that your ability to obey Allah comes from a past reservoir rather than from His continuous giving? What practical step can you take today to live in awareness of that simultaneity?

Why Power Must Be Concurrent with the Act
Al-Nasafi refutes the claim that power precedes the act with three arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's three arguments refuting the claim that power precedes the act, and why power must be the concurrent effective cause.

Core Idea
If the act occurs without power, power is useless and the act proves incapacity.

Al-Nasafi now directly confronts the Mu'tazila claim that power (qudra) precedes the act. He offers three arguments showing this view leads to absurd consequences, ultimately undermining the very proof of God's power that theologians rely on. This lesson walks through his logical refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage Carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let al-Nasafi's argument unfold naturally.
Notice how he uses rhetorical questions to dismantle the opponent's position.
2
Understand the First Objection
Identify the initial argument: if the act can exist without power, what benefit does power have? The opponent must either admit power is useless or deny power entirely.
3
Examine the Instruments Analogy
Al-Nasafi compares created power to deficient power that needs instruments. Just as grasping without a hand is impossible, the act without concurrent power is impossible.
This analogy shows the absurdity of the opponent's position.
4
Grasp the Final Inferential Argument
The decisive point: if the act is not by power when it exists, but by it when absent, then absence of power becomes the cause. This would make the act evidence for incapacity, not power, destroying the proof of God's power and tawhid.
This is the strongest argument, tying the issue directly to theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم: لما كان الفعل متصور الوجود مع انعدام القدرة بل هو واجب الوجود في هذه الحالة، فأي فائدة لوجود القدرة؟ وأي حاجة إليها؟ وأي أثر لوجودها سابقة على الفعل ولا تعلق له بها ويجب وجوده مع عدمها؟ فقولوا لا قدرة البتة إذ لا يقول بوجودها من يقول إلا لضرورة حصول الفعل بها، فإذا كان يستحيل وجوده بها، ويجب وجوده مع عدمها أو ثبوت ضدها، كان القول بنفيها أصلاً أحق وأصوب. ثم نقول: لما كانت القدرة المحدثة ناقصة ولم يكن بد من وجود الآلات والأسباب لتكمله هي، إذ الآلة أعدت لتكميل القدرة الناقصة، ولهذا يستحيل أن يكون الله تعالى فاعلاً بالآلة؛ لأن قدرته كاملة غير ناقصة فكانت مستغنية عما يكمل به، ثم لو جاز وجود الفعل مع انعدام حقيقة القدرة جاز أيضا مع انعدام ما أعد تتميمًا لها فيقبض الإنسان حال عدم اليد، ويمشي حال عدم الرجل، ويقطع حال عدم السكين، وحيث استحال ذلك وإن كانت هذه الآلات موجودة قبل ذلك بلا فصل فكذا في حقيقة القدرة. وفساد هذا مما لا يخفى على من رزق أدنى لب، فكذا هذا. والذي يقرر ذلك: أن القدرة لو لم يكن بها فعل وهي موجودة ويكون بها وهي غير موجودة فيكون سبب وجود الفعل عدم القدرة لا وجودها، فيصير القول به قولا بوجود الفعل لعدم القدرة، فيكون الفعل دليلاً على أن ليس الفاعل بقادر ولا على أنه قادر، وبالفعل استدلوا على أن الله تعالى قادر، فبطل موضع الاستدلال بالشاهد وقع على العكس، وكان ينبغي أن يستدل بوجود الفعل على أن الفاعل ليس بقادر، وفيه بطلان القول بالتوحيد، ولأن القدرة إذا كانت لا تنفع وهي موجودة، فوجودها وقت الوجود وعدمها بمنزلة كانت أولى أن لا تنفع وهي معدومة، وفي ذلك لزوم القول بالفعل من غير القدرة وإهدارها، وهذا محال.
Then it is said to them: Since the act is conceivable of existence with the absence of power, rather it is necessary of existence in this state, what benefit is there for the existence of power? And what need is there for it? And what effect is there for its existence preceding the act when it has no connection to it and its existence is necessary with its absence? So say that there is no power at all, since no one affirms its existence except due to the necessity of the act's occurrence by it. So if its existence is impossible with it, and its existence is necessary with its absence or the establishment of its opposite, then the statement denying it altogether is more fitting and correct. Then we say: Since created power is deficient, and there must be the existence of instruments and causes to complete it – for the instrument is prepared to complete the deficient power – for this reason it is impossible for God, exalted, to act through an instrument, because His power is perfect, not deficient, so it is independent of what completes it. Then, if the existence of the act were permissible with the absence of the reality of power, it would also be permissible with the absence of what is prepared to complete it, so a person would grasp when the hand is absent, walk when the leg is absent, and cut when the knife is absent. Since that is impossible even if these instruments existed immediately before that, so too regarding the reality of power. The corruption of this is not hidden from one who possesses the least intellect, and so too this. And what establishes that is: that if the act is not by power while it exists, and it is by it while it does not exist, then the cause of the act's existence is the absence of power, not its existence. Thus, this statement becomes a statement that the act exists due to the absence of power, so the act becomes evidence that the agent is not powerful, nor that he is powerful. Yet they used the act to infer that God, exalted, is powerful, so the place of inference (al-istidlāl) from the witnessed becomes invalid and turns to the opposite. It would be necessary to infer from the act's existence that the agent is not powerful, and in that is the invalidation of the statement of tawḥīd. And because when power is not beneficial while it exists, its existence at the time of existence and its absence are equivalent, it is more fitting that it not be beneficial while it is non-existent. In that is the necessary consequence of affirming the act without power and disregarding it, and this is impossible.
Source pages p. 809

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that power precedes the act. The author presents an objection to the opponent: if the act can exist without power (i.e., when power is absent), then what purpose does power serve? The opponent must either deny power altogether or accept that power is unnecessary. The author then argues that created power is deficient and requires instruments (ālāt). If the act could occur without the reality of power, it could also occur without instruments—like grasping without a hand. Since that is absurd, so is the act without concurrent power. Finally, a decisive argument: if the act occurs not by power when it exists, but by it when it does not exist, then the actual cause of the act is the absence of power. This would make the act evidence for the agent's incapacity, not power. Since Muslim theologians use the act to prove God's power, this would undermine tawḥīd. Moreover, if power is useless when present, its presence and absence are equal, leading to the absurdity of an act without any power.

Key Terms
القدرة (power)
الفعل (act)
الآلات (instruments)
التوحيد (tawhid)
الاستدلال (inference)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Power is a passive prerequisite that does not need to be concurrent with the act.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that if power were passive, it could be absent while the act occurs, leading to absurd consequences. Power must be the effective concurrent cause.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi's final argument, if the act is not by power when it exists and is by it when it does not exist, what does this imply about the act as evidence?
A) The act proves the agent is powerful.
B) The act proves the agent is incapable.
C) The act proves nothing about the agent.
D) The act proves the agent is both powerful and incapable.

Key Takeaway
Power must be the concurrent effective cause of the act; otherwise, the act would prove incapacity, not power, destroying the proof of God's power and tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own life, do you recognize moments where you assumed your actions were disconnected from your own power and responsibility? How does the necessity of concurrent power in this lesson challenge your excuse-making for sin?
?
If the act proves the power of the agent, what does your daily worship—or lack of it—actually prove about your heart's power and commitment? Are you content with an inconsistency that would make the act evidence of incapacity?
?
Al-Nasafi argues that if power is useless, then asserting it is pointless. What 'power' do you claim to have over your life that you never actually use? Will you repent from claiming faith without action?

The Mu'tazilite Position Leads to Compulsion (Jabr)
Imam Nasafi argues that Mu'tazilite denial of power at action time implies compulsion and jabr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying power at the time of action forces the conclusion that actions occur under compulsion, contradicting the Mu'tazilite rejection of jabr.

Core Idea
Denying power at action time is the essence of jabr.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi builds on the previous proof to expose a critical flaw in the Mu'tazilite view. He argues that if power is absent at the moment of action, the action is no different from one occurring after the loss of instruments—both are compelled. This forces the Mu'tazila into the very position they reject.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to follow the logical flow.
The passage is a continuation of an earlier argument.
2
Understand the analogy with power before/after action
Imam Nasafi shows that power before or after is equally useless if not present at action time.
This strengthens the earlier point.
3
Grasp the comparison with loss of instruments
Just as action after instruments fail is compelled, so is action without power.
The author says 'بل أولى' because power is more essential than instruments.
4
See the conclusion: the Mu'tazila inadvertently affirm jabr
By calling such compelled actions 'friends of God', they endorse jabr.
This is a powerful reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أنها إذا لم تكن موجودة وقت الفعل فلا فرق بين قدرة توجد قبل الفعل وبين قدرة توجد بعد الفعل لاستوائهما في العدم وقت الفعل، والقول بكونها بعد الفعل محال، فكذا هذا. ومما يبين سفه المعتزلة وجهلهم بالحقائق أن الفعل لو كان يقع ولا قدرة عليه للفاعل وقت وقوعه لكان وقوعه عن اضطرار، ألا يُرَى أنه لو وقع بعد ارتفاع صحة الآلات لكان واقعًا عن اضطرار، فكذا هذا. بل أولى إذ حصول الفعل بالقدرة دون صحة الأسباب. ثم إن المعتزلة صيروا العهد بهذا الفصل الواقع عن اضطرار وليا لله تعالى وعدوا له وهذا هو القول بالجبر. ثم إنهم إن لم يجعلوه وقت الفصل مأموراً منهيًا بهذا الفعل فقد أخرجوه عن كونه طاعة ومعصية وفاعله عن كونه مطيعا وعاصيًا، وفيه إبطال الأوامر والنواهي ورفع الشرائع وإزالة الحل والحرمة، وهذا خروج عن الملة ودخول في قول منكري الشرائع وإبطال العداوة والولاية، وفيه وصف الله تعالى بكونه ظالما بتعذيبه على فعل من هذه الأفعال، وإن جعلوه وقت الفعل مأمورًا منهيًا، فقد وصفوا الله تعالى بالسفه، حيث أمر بما كان العبد مضطرًا إليه عاجزا عنه أو نهى عنه. والذي يقرر هذا: أن العبد لو كان مأمورًا بالفعل أو منهيًا عنه وقت وجود [؟] والفعل عنه في تلك الحالة مستحيل فكان مأمورًا بما يستحيل وجوده، منهيًا عما يمنع ثبوته، وهذا محال وإن كان مأمورًا وقت القدرة ليفعل بها في الثاني، لم القدرة [؟]
He establishes that if it is not present at the time of the action, then there is no difference between power existing before the action and power existing after the action because both are equally nonexistent at the time of the action, and saying it exists after the action is impossible, so this is likewise. And what shows the foolishness of the Mu'tazila and their ignorance of realities is that if an action were to occur without the agent having power over it at the time of its occurrence, it would occur under compulsion. Do you not see that if it occurred after the validity of the instruments had ceased, it would occur under compulsion? So likewise this. Rather it is more fitting since the action occurs through power, not through the validity of causes. Then the Mu'tazila made the covenant in this chapter that what occurs under compulsion is a friend of God Almighty and they counted it as such, and this is the statement of jabr. Then if they do not consider him at the time of the occurrence commanded or prohibited regarding this action, they have removed it from being obedience or disobedience and the agent from being obedient or disobedient. In this is the invalidation of commands and prohibitions, the lifting of laws, the removal of the lawful and unlawful. This is exit from the religion and entry into the statement of the deniers of laws, and the invalidation of enmity and friendship. In it is the description of God Almighty as being unjust by punishing for such actions. And if they consider him at the time of the action commanded or prohibited, they have described God Almighty as foolish, because He commanded what the servant is compelled to and powerless from, or prohibited him from it. What establishes this: that if the servant were commanded with an action or prohibited from it at the time of existence [?] and the action from him in that state is impossible, then he would be commanded with what is impossible to exist and prohibited from what prevents its confirmation, and this is impossible. And if he were commanded at the time of power to do it in the second [moment], the power [؟]
Source pages p. 811

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazilite position by drawing out its disastrous consequences. The author first strengthens the earlier proof: if power is absent at the time of action, then power before and after are equally useless, and saying power exists after action is absurd. Next, he argues that without power at the moment, the action is compelled (idṭirār), just as action after the failure of instruments is compelled. The Mu'tazila would thus be endorsing jabr (compulsion) by making such action a 'friend of God'. Then he presents a dilemma: either the agent is considered commanded/prohibited at the time of action or not. If not, then the action cannot be obedience or disobedience, nullifying all commands, prohibitions, laws, and making God unjust for punishing. If yes, then God commands the impossible, which is foolishness. The latter is impossible, so the Mu'tazilite position is self-defeating.

Key Terms
اضطرار
جبر
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mu'tazila avoid jabr because they affirm power before action.
Correction: Imam Nasafi shows that power before action is irrelevant if not present at action time; the action is still compelled.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude about the Mu'tazilite position on power?
A) It avoids jabr.
B) It leads to jabr.
C) It is consistent.
D) It is based on reason.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite denial of power at the time of action forces them into the very doctrine of compulsion they oppose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever made excuses for your own sins by blaming circumstances or your past, effectively denying that you had the power to choose otherwise at that moment? How does this lesson expose the spiritual danger of such thinking?
?
If you truly believed that God holds you accountable only for actions over which you have real power at the instant you do them, would you become more vigilant in guarding your heart and intentions? What would change in your daily routine?
?
The Mu'tazila ended up affirming the very jabr they rejected. In your own life, are there beliefs or habits you cling to that, if taken to their logical end, undermine your faith? Will you examine one such belief today and see if it leads away from God?

The Dilemma of Divine Commands Without Power
Imam Nasafi presents a dilemma that Mu'tazilite view on power undermines divine commands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how the Mu'tazilite view leads to an untenable choice: either divine commands become meaningless or God commands the impossible.

Core Idea
Without power at action, commands are either invalid or impossible.

Having shown that the Mu'tazilite position on power leads to compulsion, Imam Nasafi now presents a devastating dilemma regarding divine commands. He argues that if the agent is considered commanded or prohibited at the time of action despite lacking power, then either the action cannot be a valid act of obedience/disobedience (rendering all laws null) or God commands the impossible. Both options are absurd.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma passage
Focus on the two options: either the agent is considered commanded at time of action or not.
The passage uses 'إن لم يجعلوه' and 'إن جعلوه'.
2
Understand the first horn: no command at action time
If not commanded at action time, the action is not obedience/disobedience, nullifying all sharia.
This also makes God unjust for punishing.
3
Understand the second horn: command at action time
If commanded at action time, then God commands the impossible since the agent lacks power.
This attributes foolishness (safah) to God.
4
See the conclusion: Mu'tazilite position is self-defeating
Both options are impossible, so the position is false.
The author mentions the absurd consequence of nullifying laws.
