A) Because Zaid does not actually go
B) Because the action is attributed to Zaid only as a description of what happens to him
C) Because Zaid has no will
D) Because only God can cause motion

Key Takeaway
The Jabriyya view reduces all human actions to involuntary events directly created by God, with human agency being merely metaphorical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Think of a daily action you do — like praying or helping someone. Do you truly feel it is your action, or do you sometimes feel it is just something happening to you? What would change if you fully believed that every good deed is an act you are responsible for? Write a short resolve to reclaim ownership of one action today.
?
The Jabriyya say saying 'Zaid went' is like saying 'the tree grew' — no real agency. Is there any part of your life where you live as if your choices are just events, not real decisions? Will you embrace the accountability that Ash'aris and Ahl al-Sunna affirm: that your actions are truly yours even though Allah creates them? Make a concrete pledge to stop pretending you have no control in a specific situation.

The Mu'tazila View on Human Creation
Al-Nasafi presents the Mu'tazila view and its radicalization through history.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila doctrine that humans create their own actions independently of God's will, and the historical progression of their terminology from 'bringer-into-existence' to 'creator'.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila claimed humans are true creators, progressively denying God's creative power.

In this passage, al-Nasafi lays out the Mu'tazila position on human actions and traces how their vocabulary evolved. He shows that early Mu'tazila hesitated to call the servant a creator, but later figures like al-Jubba'i and al-Ja'd became bolder, eventually claiming God is only metaphorically a creator. This sets the stage for understanding a key theological dispute about human free will and divine omnipotence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Notice how al-Nasafi presents the Mu'tazila doctrine and then gives a historical account. Pay attention to the shift in terminology.
The passage contains a narrative of three stages.
2
Identify the three stages
Find the early Mu'tazila, Abu Ali al-Jubba'i, and al-Ja'd al-Basri. What did each affirm about human creative power?
3
Analyze the doctrine
According to the Mu'tazila, do humans create independently of God's will? What terms did they use?
They said actions occur whether God wills or not.
4
Reflect on the implications
How does this view challenge Islamic consensus on God as the sole creator? What is al-Nasafi's condemnation?
Al-Nasafi ends with a strong condemnation.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to consolidate what you've learned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول المعتزلة بالاختيار: وبعضهم جعلوها العباد وقطعوا تدبير الله عنها بالكلية، وقالوا: يخترعها العباد فيخرجونها من العدم إلى الوجود ويحدثونها، ويقولون: إيجادها وإحداثها شاء الله تعالى ذلك أم لم يشأ، وإليه ذهبت المعتزلة القدرية بأجمعهم، إلا أن أوائلهم كانوا يتحرجون عن إطلاق لفظة التخليق وتسمية العبد خالقا، وكانوا يطابقون جميع المسلمين في قولهم: لا خالق إلا الله وإن كانوا يثبتون معنى الخلق كانوا يطلقون لفظة الإيجاد والإحداث، ويسمون العبد موجدًا محدثًا إلى زمن أبي علي الجبائي، فلما رأى معنى الخلق ثابتًا أطلق لفظة الخالق وسمي العبد خالقًا، ولم يبال من مخالفة إجماع الأمة مع إقراره بكونه حجة موجبة للعلم قطعًا كالنص لما رأى من تحير وعجزهم عن التفرقة بين الإيجاد والتخليق، وكان الناس يتعجبون من جرأته على الله تعالى وركوبه حطة مخالفة إجماع المسلمين ليتمكن من تحقيق ضلالاته إلى أن نشأ أبو عبد الله البصري المعروف بالجعد منهم وأتى بما لم يتجاسر عليه مشرك، فزعم أن الله تعالى ليس بخالق في الحقيقة بل يوصف بذلك مجازا وإنما الخالق على الحقيقة هو العبد - تعالى الله عما يقول الظالمون علوا كبيرًا.
The doctrine of the Mu'tazila of choice: And some of them made them [belong to] the servants and completely cut off God's management from them, and said: The servants invent them, bringing them out from non-existence to existence and causing them to occur, and they say: Their bringing into existence and occurrence occurs whether God wills that or not, and this is the position of all the Qadari Mu'tazila, except that their early ones used to hesitate to apply the term 'creation' (takhliq) and to call the servant a creator (khaliq), and they used to agree with all Muslims in their saying: There is no creator but Allah, even though they affirmed the meaning of creation; they used to apply the term 'bringing into existence' (ijad) and 'causing to occur' (ihdath), and they used to call the servant a bringer-into-existence (mujid) and a causer-of-occurrence (muhdith) until the time of Abu Ali al-Jubba'i. When he saw that the meaning of creation is established, he applied the term 'creator' and called the servant a creator, and he did not care about opposing the consensus of the ummah while acknowledging it to be a proof necessitating knowledge definitively like the text, because he saw their confusion and inability to differentiate between bringing into existence and creation. People used to marvel at his audacity against Allah and his embarking upon the grave matter of opposing the consensus of Muslims in order to achieve his misguidances, until Abu Abdullah al-Basri known as al-Ja'd arose among them and came with what no polytheist had dared, claiming that Allah is not a creator in reality but is described as such metaphorically, and that the real creator is the servant – exalted is Allah above what the wrongdoers say, a great exaltation.

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazila doctrine of choice (ikhtiyar) regarding human actions. They claim servants create their own actions independently of God's will. Al-Nasafi then gives a historical account: early Mu'tazila avoided calling the servant a creator, using 'bringer-into-existence' instead, until Abu Ali al-Jubba'i openly used 'creator'. Later, al-Ja'd went further, claiming God is not truly a creator but only metaphorically. The passage ends with a condemnation of this view.

The Shared False Premise of Jabriyya and Mu'tazila
Al-Nasafi identifies the shared false premise underlying both extreme doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the agreement on a false premise about divine and human agency led to the contradictory extremes of Jabriyya and Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
One false premise about agency gave rise to both deterministic and libertarian extremes.

Al-Nasafi uncovers the surprising root of two opposing sects: they share a common but mistaken assumption. Before reading, consider how disagreement can sometimes mask deeper agreement on a flawed foundation. This passage reveals that both Jabriyya and Mu'tazila started from the same error.

Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic and translation to grasp the argument.
The passage is incomplete but the key point is clear.

Note that they argue from the witnessed world to the unseen.
3
Understand the branching
Notice how the Mu'tazila took one path (focusing on human agency) while the Jabriyya took the opposite path (divine agency alone).
The passage cuts off before detailing the Jabriyya's path, but the implication is clear.

سبب بطلان قول الجبرية والمعتزلة: وإنما تفرع هذان المذهبان الباطلان المتناقضان أعني مذهب الجبرية ومذهب القدرية الحاصلين على طرفي الغلو والتقصير من اتفاق الفريقين على مقدمة كاذبة، وهي أن دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين محال، لما وجدوا ذلك في الشاهد محالاً، والشاهد أصل الغائب، فبعد ذلك نظرت المعتزلة إلى الدلائل الموجبة كون العباد فاعلين قادرين فتمسكوا بها، وجعلوا أفعال العباد

After that, the Mu'tazila looked to the proofs that require that servants are agents and capable, so they adhered to them, and they made the actions of the servants...
Source pages p. 850

Commentary
This passage explains the shared false premise that led to both extreme doctrines. Al-Nasafi states that the Jabriyya and Mu'tazila, despite their opposition, both agreed on a false assumption: that one action cannot be under the power of two agents simultaneously. They argued from the witnessed world, which is the basis for understanding the unseen. From this premise, each group took a different path: the Mu'tazila focused on proofs of human agency and concluded that humans create their own actions, while the Jabriyya (implied) focused on divine omnipotence and concluded that God is the sole agent. The passage cuts off before completing the explanation.

The Shared False Premise of Jabariyya and Qadariyya
Nasafi identifies the shared false premise that leads to both Jabari and Qadari errors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the shared false premise that leads to both Jabari and Qadari errors and how each group errs in its response.

Core Idea
One false premise produces two opposite errors: Jabariyya and Qadariyya.

Nasafi reveals a surprising insight: the two opposing sects, Jabariyya (extreme predestinarians) and Qadariyya (Mu'tazila advocating free will), actually agree on a fundamental false premise. This agreement then leads each group to adopt extreme positions by focusing on different evidence while ignoring contradictory proofs. This passage explores that false premise and the resulting errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shared false premise
Read the passage to find the premise that both groups agree on. Note how Nasafi states it and why he calls it false.
The premise concerns the impossibility of one act being under two powers.
2
Follow the Mu'tazila response
Observe how the Mu'tazila used this premise to argue that human actions are created by humans and outside God's power, ignoring proofs of God's all-encompassing power.
3
Follow the Jabariyya response
See how the Jabariyya used the same premise to deny any power to humans, making all actions involuntary, and ignoring proofs of human agency.
They also argued that any power not attaching to an act would be indistinguishable from incapacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سبب بطلان قول الجبرية والمعتزلة

وإنما تفرع هذان المذهبان الباطلان المتناقضان أعني مذهب الجبرية ومذهب القدرية الحاصلين على طرفي الغلو والتقصير من اتفاق الفريقين على مقدمة كاذبة، وهى أن دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين محال، لما وجدوا ذلك في الشاهد محالاً، والشاهد أصل الغائب، فبعد ذلك نظرت المعتزلة إلى الدلائل الموجبة كون العباد فاعلين قادرين فتمسكوا بها، وجعلوا أفعال العباد الداخلة تحت قدرتهم مخلوقة لهم خارجة عن قدرة الله تعالى وعموا عن الدلائل التي توجب إحالة خروج مقدور عن قدرة الله تعالى.

ونظرت الجبرية إلى الدلائل الموجبة دخول هذه الأفعال تحت قدرة الله تعالى المثبتة إحالة ثبوت قدرة التخليق لغير الباري جل وعلا، فتمسكوا بتلك الدلائل وجعلوا الأفعال مخلوقة لله تعالى خارجة عن أن تكون مقدوره لغيره لاستحالة تعلق قدرة غير الله تعالى بما تعلقت به قدرة الله تعالى.

ثم لما لم يتصور عندهم مقدور لا تعلق له بقدرة الله تعالى لا يتصور أن يتعلق مقدور ما بمقدور غير الله تعالى ولو كانت لغير الله تعالى قدرة لكانت قدرة لا يتصور تعلقها بمقدور ما البتة، ومن المحال وجود قدرة لا يتصور تعلقها بمقدور إذ لم يكن حينئذ بينهما وبين العجز فرق، أبوا على هذه القضية أن تكون لغير الله تعالى قدرة، وجعلوا أفعال الحيوانات كلها اضطرارية، وعموا عن الدلائل الموجبة أن يكون للعباد فعل وأن لهم القدرة على أفعالهم.
The cause of the invalidity of the saying of the Jabariyya and the Mu'tazila

These two false and contradictory doctrines, namely the doctrine of the Jabariyya and the doctrine of the Qadariyya, which have reached the two extremes of excess and deficiency, only branched out from the agreement of both groups on a false premise: that it is impossible for a single possible act to fall under the power of two capable agents. Since they found that impossible in the witnessed world (al-shāhid), and the witnessed is the basis for the unseen (al-ghāʼib). After that, the Mu'tazila looked at the proofs that require that servants be agents and capable, so they clung to them, and they made the actions of servants that fall under their power created by them, outside the power of God Almighty, and they were blind to the proofs that require the impossibility of an act falling outside the power of God Almighty.

And the Jabariyya looked at the proofs that require the entry of these actions under the power of God Almighty, which establish the impossibility of establishing the power of creation for other than the Creator, so they clung to those proofs and made the actions created by God Almighty, outside of being possible for other than Him, due to the impossibility of the attachment of the power of other than God to what the power of God has attached to.

Then, since for them it is inconceivable that an act exists that has no relation to God's power, and it is inconceivable that any act attaches to the power of other than God — and if there were a power for other than God, it would be a power that cannot attach itself to any act at all, and it is impossible for a power that cannot attach to any act to exist, for then there would be no difference between it and incapacity — they rejected on the basis of this issue that there be any power for other than God, and they made all actions of animals involuntary, and they were blind to the proofs that require that servants have action and that they have power over their actions.
Source pages p. 850

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of the shared false premise that underlies both the Jabariyya (extreme predestinarians) and the Qadariyya (Mu'tazila capacity advocates). It begins by stating that both contradictory groups agree on a false premise: that one act cannot be under the power of two agents. They mistakenly base this on the witnessed world (shāhid) and analogize to the unseen. 

First, the Mu'tazila focused on evidence that humans are agents and capable, so they adopted that and claimed human actions are created by humans, outside God's power, ignoring evidence that nothing can escape God's power.

Second, the Jabariyya focused on evidence that all actions are under God's power, which implies that no one else can have creative power. They concluded that actions are only created by God and cannot be possible acts for others, because that would require a power for others that attaches to the same act, which they deem impossible. They further argued that if there were a power for others, it would be a power that attaches to no act (since all acts are already under God's power), and such a power would be indistinguishable from incapacity. Therefore they denied any power for humans, making all animal actions involuntary, and ignored evidence that humans have actions and power.

Key Terms
جبرية (Jabariyya)
قدرية (Qadariyya)
مقدمة كاذبة (false premise)
مقدور (possible act)
قدرة قادرين (power of two agents)
شاهد (witnessed)
غائب (unseen)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jabariyya and Qadariyya are completely opposite and share no common ground.
Correction: They both agree on the false premise that one act cannot be under two powers, leading to their extreme positions.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the false premise that both Jabariyya and Mu'tazila agree upon?
A) God alone is the Creator of all actions.
B) Humans have free will and create their own actions.
C) It is impossible for one possible act to be under the power of two capable agents.
D) The seen world is the basis for understanding the unseen world.

Key Takeaway
The false premise that one act cannot be under two powers is the root of both Jabari and Qadari errors; each sect selectively follows proofs that support its conclusion while ignoring others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that a false premise can lead even sincere groups to opposite errors. Are you aware of any assumption in your own life that you have never questioned, which might be shaping your beliefs in a one-sided way? What would it cost you to examine it honestly?
?
The Mu'tazila and Jabariyya each saw only the proofs that supported their view. In your relationship with Allah, do you ever focus only on verses of mercy and ignore those of warning, or vice versa? How can you train yourself to accept the full picture even when it challenges your comfort?
?
The shared false premise here is that God's control and human responsibility are mutually exclusive. Do you live as if your actions are entirely up to you, or as if you have no free will at all? How does this passage call you to a more balanced reliance on Allah while taking personal accountability for your choices?

The Ahl al-Sunna Middle Position on Human Action
Nasafi presents the Ahl al-Sunna doctrine affirming both human acquisition and divine creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Sunna affirm both human moral responsibility and divine creation of actions, avoiding the extremes of compulsion (Jabriyya) and absolute free will (Qadariyya).

Core Idea
Human actions are acquired by us but created by God – a middle path between compulsion and free will.

Nasafi presents the Ahl al-Sunna position as a balanced doctrine that affirms both human moral responsibility and God's sole creative power. This passage is crucial for understanding how Sunni theologians avoided the extremes of predestinarianism (Jabriyya) and absolute free will (Qadariyya). It introduces key concepts like the attachment of two powers to one act and the derivation of justice and bounty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two affirmations
Notice how Nasafi first affirms that actions truly belong to humans ('haqqaqa al-afʿāl'), making them obedient or disobedient, then immediately states these actions are created by God.
2
Understand the key negation
Observe the rejection of the impossibility of two powers (qadratayn) attaching to one possible act (maqdūr wāḥid). This is the technical solution that allows both human and divine agency.
This is a distinctive Ashʿari-Māturīdi position.
3
Derive the theological implications
See how from the first affirmation comes justice (God is not unjust to His servants), and from the second comes bounty (God's grace).
These two results ground the doctrine of just reward and punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق وقال : إنهم بها صاروا عصاة مطيعين وجعلوها مخلوقة الله تعالى، ونفوا إحالة تعلق قدرتين بمقدور واحد، ونفوا الضرورة عن أفعالهم، وبدخولها تحت قدرة الباري جل وعلا، فيستفاد بالأول ثبوت العدل ونفي الظلم تحقيقا لقوله تعالى: وَمَا رَبُّكَ بِظَلَّامٍ لِلْعَبِيدِ وإثبات الفضل
And among them is one who affirmed actions for creation and said: through them they become disobedient and obedient, and he made them created by God Almighty, and he negated the impossibility of the attachment of two powers to a single possible act, and negated compulsion (al-ḍarūra) from their actions, and [affirmed] their entry under the power of the Creator. So from the first is derived the establishment of justice and the negation of injustice, in realization of His saying: 'And your Lord is not unjust to His servants' (41:46), and the establishment of bounty.
Source pages p. 851

Commentary
This passage is a concise statement of the Ahl al-Sunna position on human actions. It begins by saying that the salaf (or the Ahl al-Sunna) fully affirmed actions for the creation (al-khalq), i.e., humans. They stated that through these actions humans become obedient or disobedient, thus establishing moral responsibility. However, they also affirmed that these actions are created by God Almighty (makhluqa li-llāh). This is not seen as contradictory because they rejected the impossibility of two powers (qadratayn) attaching to one possible act (maqdūr wāḥid). They also negated compulsion (al-ḍarūra) from human actions, meaning humans are not forced. They affirmed that actions fall under the power of the Creator. From the first point (affirming human action) comes the establishment of justice (al-ʿadl) and negation of injustice (al-ẓulm), as God is not unjust to His servants. From the second point (affirming divine creation) comes the establishment of bounty (al-faḍl), i.e., God's grace.

قدرتين (qadratayn)
مقدور واحد (maqdūr wāḥid)
ضرورة (ḍarūra)
عدل (ʿadl)
فضل (faḍl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ahl al-Sunna deny human action entirely.
Correction: They affirm human acquisition and responsibility while maintaining divine creation.

Checkpoint
According to the Ahl al-Sunna position described by Nasafi, how do humans become obedient or disobedient?
A) Through actions that they create independently of God.
B) Through actions that are created by God but which they acquire.
C) Through actions that are entirely forced upon them by God.
D) Through actions that are only attributed to them metaphorically.

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna reconcile human responsibility and divine power by affirming that actions are truly acquired by humans yet created by God, preserving both justice and grace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly feel the weight of your own responsibility, or do you find yourself subtly blaming your circumstances or God's decree? How does this lesson's teaching that your actions are acquired by you yet created by God challenge your tendency to deflect accountability?
?
Your Lord is not unjust to His servants. If you ever felt that God was unfair to you, how would this passage force you to reconsider your own role in your trials?
?
The passage says from divine creation comes the establishment of bounty. Do you genuinely thank God for empowering your good deeds, or do you silently credit yourself? What would it mean to live with constant gratitude for every action you take?

The Errors of Mu'tazila and Jabriyya on Human Actions
Critique of Mu'tazila and Jabriyya on human action and divine power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why both the Mu'tazila and Jabriyya positions on human actions are erroneous according to Maturidi theology.

Core Idea
Both extremes—denying God's power or denying human power—are blind to full evidence.

This passage exposes the blind spots of two influential sects. The Mu'tazila overemphasized human power, while the Jabriyya overemphasized divine power. The author shows how each group ignored key proofs, leading to doctrinal error. Let's see the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's critique of both groups sink in.
Notice the parallel structure: both groups are described as 'blind' to proofs.
2
Identify the two groups and their claims
Find where the Mu'tazila claim is stated (actions created by humans, outside God's power) and where the Jabriyya claim is stated (actions created by God, no power for others).
3
Trace the reasoning of each group
The Mu'tazila ignore proofs that nothing can be outside God's power. The Jabriyya argue that any power for others would be inconceivable. Understand the logic behind each error.
The Jabriyya use a reductio ad absurdum: if another had power, it would be useless (indistinguishable from incapacity).
4
Reflect on the Maturidi middle path
Consider that the author implies a balanced view: human actions are both within divine power and genuinely attributable to humans. This lesson prepares you for the correct position.
The middle path avoids both extremes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الداخلة تحت قدرتهم مخلوقة لهم خارجة عن قدرة الله تعالى وعموا عن الدلائل التي توجب إحالة خروج مقدور عن قدرة الله تعالى. ونظرت الجبرية إلى الدلائل الموجبة دخول هذه الأفعال تحت قدرة الله تعالى المثبتة إحالة ثبوت قدرة التخليق لغير الباري جل وعلا، فتمسكوا بتلك الدلائل وجعلوا الأفعال مخلوقة لله تعالى خارجة عن أن تكون مقدوره لغيره لاستحالة تعلق قدرة غير الله تعالى بما تعلقت به قدرة الله تعالى ثم لما لم يتصور عندهم مقدور لا تعلق له بقدرة الله تعالى لا يتصور أن يتعلق مقدور ما بمقدور غير الله تعالى ولو كانت لغير الله تعالى قدرة لكانت قدرة لا يتصور تعلقها بمقدور ما البتة، ومن المحال وجود قدرة لا يتصور تعلقها بمقدور إذ لم يكن حينئذ بينهما وبين العجز فرق، أبوا على هذه القضية أن تكون لغير الله تعالى قدرة، وجعلوا أفعال الحيوانات كلها اضطرارية، وعموا عن الدلائل الموجبة أن يكون للعباد فعل وأن لهم القدرة على أفعالهم.
Those actions that fall under their power are created by them and outside the power of Allah, and they were blind to the proofs that necessitate the impossibility of an object of power exiting from the power of Allah. And the Jabriyya looked at the proofs that necessitate the entry of these actions under the power of Allah, which affirm the impossibility of establishing the power of creation for other than the Exalted Creator, so they clung to those proofs and made actions created by Allah, outside being possible objects of power for other than Him, due to the impossibility of the power of other than Allah being attached to what the power of Allah is attached to. Then, since in their view it is inconceivable that there be an object of power not related to the power of Allah, it is inconceivable that any object of power be related to the power of other than Allah, and if there were a power for other than Allah, it would be a power whose attachment to any object of power is inconceivable, and the existence of a power whose attachment to an object of power is inconceivable is impossible, since then there would be no difference between it and incapacity. So they denied, on this basis, that there is a power for other than Allah, and they made all the actions of animals involuntary, and they were blind to the proofs that necessitate that servants have action and that they have power over their actions.
Source pages p. 851

Commentary
This passage defines the errors of two extreme groups. First, the Mu'tazila claimed that human actions are created by humans and outside God's power, ignoring proofs that show it's impossible for any object of power to be outside God's power. Second, the Jabriyya focused only on proofs that all actions are under God's power, concluding that no one else can have any power, making all actions involuntary. Both groups are described as 'blind' to the full evidence. The author presents the Jabriyya's reasoning: if any power existed for other than Allah, it would be a power that cannot attach to any object of power, making it indistinguishable from incapacity, so they deny any power for others. Thus they fall into determinism.

Key Terms
قدرة
مقدور
جبرية
معتزلة
خلق الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why did the Jabriyya deny any power for non-divine beings?
A) Because they believed that any power besides God's would be independent and thus a rival.
B) Because they thought that if a power existed for other than Allah, it would be unable to attach to any object of power, making it useless and indistinguishable from incapacity.
C) Because they followed the Mu'tazila in denying human power.
D) Because they considered human actions as metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
Both the Mu'tazila and Jabriyya erred by focusing on only part of the evidence, leading to extremes that contradict the balanced Maturidi view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you tend to blame your circumstances or Allah's decree (like the Jabriyya), or do you fully acknowledge your own responsibility? Today, commit to taking ownership of one specific action you've been excusing.
?
Are there areas of your life where you act as if you are completely independent of Allah's power (like the Mu'tazila)? Choose one area—your career, health, or relationships—and consciously remind yourself today that every outcome is under His control.
?
Both sects were blinded by partial truths. What partial truth about Allah's power or your own ability are you clinging to that prevents you from seeing the full picture? Resolve to seek the balanced understanding that honors both divine sovereignty and human accountability.

The Sunni Doctrine on Human Actions and Its Divine Benefits
The author enumerates the Sunni doctrine and its two benefits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni (Maturidi) position on human actions: that they are created by Allah yet belong to humans, and the theological benefits of this doctrine.

Core Idea
Human actions are both created by Allah and truly ours - this establishes justice and grace.

In this passage, the author outlines the core Sunni doctrine regarding human actions. He affirms that actions are real for humans, that they are created by Allah, and that both divine and human power can coexist on a single act. Then he explains the twin benefits of this doctrine: establishing divine justice and grace, and affirming Allah's description as Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the key claims
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the five doctrinal affirmations: actions belong to humans, they become obedient/disobedient, actions are created by Allah, two powers can coexist, actions are not compelled but fall under divine power.
2
Understand the two benefits
The passage says that from the first part (affirmation of human action) come justice and grace. From the second part (divine creation) comes knowledge of Allah's attributes. See how each is supported by a Quranic verse.
3
Reflect on the balance
Ask yourself why both human action and divine creation are affirmed. How does this balance avoid compulsion on one hand and independent power on the other?
This is the key to Sunni doctrine.
4
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to test your grasp of the first benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة] ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق وقال : إنهم بها صاروا عصاة مطيعين وجعلوها مخلوقة الله تعالى، ونفوا إحالة تعلق قدرتين بمقدور واحد، ونفوا الضرورة عن أفعالهم، وبدخولها تحت قدرة الباري جل وعلا، فيستفاد بالأول ثبوت العدل ونفي الظلم تحقيقا لقوله تعالى: وَمَا رَبُّكَ بِظَلَّامٍ لِلْعَبِيدِ () وإثبات الفضل تحقيقا لقوله تعالى: وَلَوْلَا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ ) . ويستفاد بالثاني معرفة بأن الله تعالى موصوف بما وصف به نفسه محمود به كما قال تعالى ( خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ وَكيل ) . هذا هو مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة.
[The doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a] And among them are those who affirmed actions for the creation and said: by them they become disobedient and obedient, and they made them created by Allah, and they denied the impossibility of two powers attaching to one object of power, and they denied compulsion in their actions, and [affirmed] their entry under the power of the Exalted Creator. So from the first benefit is established justice and the negation of injustice, in realization of His statement: 'And your Lord is not unjust to His servants' (Quran 41:46), and the affirmation of grace in realization of His statement: 'And were it not for the grace of Allah upon you and His mercy' (Quran 24:10). And from the second benefit is gained the knowledge that Allah is described with what He described Himself, praised by it, as He said: 'He created everything and He is over all things a Guardian' (Quran 39:62). This is the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.
Source pages p. 851

Commentary
This passage defines the correct Sunni doctrine. The key points: (1) Actions are affirmed for humans; through them they become obedient or disobedient. (2) Actions are created by Allah. (3) It is not impossible for two powers (divine and human) to attach to one object of power. (4) Human actions are not compelled (not involuntary). (5) Human actions fall under God's power. From the first benefit (affirming human action) comes justice: God is not unjust because humans have choice, and grace: God's favor is real. From the second benefit (creation by Allah) comes the knowledge that Allah is described as Creator and Guardian, praised accordingly. The passage ends by stating this is the Sunni doctrine.

Correction: The Sunni doctrine affirms both: actions are created by Allah yet truly belong to humans.

A) It establishes that God creates everything.
B) It establishes God's justice and negates injustice, and affirms grace.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni doctrine balances human accountability with divine creation, establishing both justice and grace.

The Ash'ari Contradiction on Human Action Terminology
Critique of Ash'ari kasb terminology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position on kasb and why the author argues it leads to a terminological contradiction.

Core Idea
Refusing to call human actions 'acts' contradicts the Quran and common speech.

In this passage, the author tackles a specific inconsistency in the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb. While both Maturidis and Ash'aris agree that God creates actions, Ash'aris insist on calling human actions 'kasb' and avoid calling them 'acts'. The author argues this is a contradiction because both the Quran and everyday Arabic use the word 'act' for human actions, and even al-Ash'ari himself uses it in his books.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to get a clear sense of the argument.
Pay attention to the Quranic quote and the mention of 'all the people of language'.
2
Identify the Ash'ari claim
Find where the author states what the Ash'aris call human actions and what they avoid calling them.
The key terms are 'kasb' and 'act' (fi'l).
3
Understand the contradiction
The author provides three pieces of evidence to show the contradiction: the Quran, common Arabic speech, and al-Ash'ari's own writings. Note each one.
Think about why using a term in one context but refusing it in another is inconsistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ مذهب الأشاعرة قريب من الماتريدية] ثم الأشعرية إن وافقونا في حقيقة المذهب فقد زعمت أن ما هو مقدور العبد يسمى كسبًا ولا يسمى فعلاً له كما لا خلقًا، يسمى وهذا منه امتناع عن إطلاق ما أطلقه الله بقوله : ( وَافَعَلُوا الخير ) وغير ذلك من الآيات، وأطلق جميع أهل اللسان قولهم: فعل فلان كذا ، وفلان كريم الفعال، وأطلق هو وجميع المتكلمين، فإن الناس بأجمعهم يسمون هذا الباب باب خلق أفعال العباد كذا ذكر الأشعري في كتبه وكذا جميع أصحابه، والامتناع عن إطلاق ما أطلق هو بنفسه تناقض، وقع
[The Ash'ari doctrine is close to the Maturidi] Then the Ash'ariyya: if they agree with us on the reality of the doctrine, they have claimed that what is the object of power of the servant is called kasb and is not called an act for him, just as it is not called creation. This is from him a refusal to apply what Allah applied in His statement: 'And do good' (Quran 22:77) and other verses. And all the people of language applied their saying: 'So-and-so did such-and-such', and 'So-and-so is generous in actions.' And he himself and all speakers apply [this]; indeed, all people call this chapter 'the chapter of the creation of the actions of servants' – thus mentioned al-Ash'ari in his books, and likewise all his companions. And refusal to apply what he himself applied is a contradiction that has occurred.
Source pages p. 852

Commentary
This passage critiques the Ash'ari position. While Ash'aris agree with Maturidis on the reality (that God creates actions), they insist on calling human actions 'kasb' (acquisition) and avoid calling them 'act' (fi'l) or 'creation' (khalq). The author argues this is an inconsistent refusal to use the same terminology that God uses (e.g., 'do good') and that all Arabic speakers use. Even al-Ash'ari himself and all speakers call this topic 'the chapter of the creation of the actions of servants'. So refusing to apply the term 'act' to human action contradicts their own usage. The passage highlights the contradiction.

Refuting Jabriyya with Quranic Evidence
Scriptural refutation of Jabriyya using Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quranic verses about commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats refute the Jabriyya doctrine of absolute determinism.

Core Idea
The Quran itself proves human responsibility for actions.

The author begins his refutation of the Jabriyya by turning to the Quran. The Book of Allah is filled with commands, prohibitions, promises of reward, and warnings of punishment—all of which would be meaningless if humans had no real agency. This passage examines several key verses and explains how they establish human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the scriptural evidence carefully
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning through the verse about justice and goodness. Focus on the verses cited and the author's commentary.
2
Identify the key Quranic proofs
List the verses mentioned: 'Do whatever you will and do good', 'Thus Allah shows them their deeds as regrets', 'Whoever does an atom's weight', 'A recompense for what they used to do'. Notice they all attribute actions to the servant.
Also note the author's point that these verses use 'workers' and 'act' in the context of command, prohibition, promise, and threat.
3
Understand the author's clarification
The author argues that attributing actions to Allah as Creator does not negate the servant's role. The servant 'acquires' and 'does' the action.
This is the Maturidi concept of kasb (acquisition).
4
Reflect on the refutation
Ask yourself: If the Jabriyya were right that humans have no choice, why would Allah command, prohibit, promise, and threaten? The Quran's very structure refutes their view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان بطلان قول الجبرية ] ومذهب الجبرية باطل بدلالة السمع والعقل والضرورة التي تصير دافع ذلك مكابرًا. فأما السمع فمن نحو قوله تعالى: اعْمَلُوا مَا شِنْتُمْ وَأَفْعَلُوا الْخَيْرَ (٣) ، وفي الجزاء : كَذَلِكَ يُرِيهِمُ اللَّهُ أَعْمَلَهُمْ حَسَرَاتٍ عَلَيْهِمْ ﴾ (٤) وقوله تعالى : ( وَمَن يَعْمَلْ (۷) ذلك مما أثبت لهم (ه) (7). ٢٤ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّة وقوله : جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ ) وغير ذلك مما أثبت لهم أسماء العمال ولفعلهم اسم الفعل بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، وليس في الإضافة إلى الله تعالى نفي ذلك بل هي الله تعالى بأن خلقها على ما وأوجدها بعد أن لم تكن، وللخلق على ما كسبوها وفعلوها على أن الله تعالى أمر ونهى ومحال الأمر بما لا فعل للمأمور أو المنهى، وقال الله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَأْمُرُ بِالْعَدْلِ وَالْإِحْسَنِ ) (۹) ولو جاز الأمر بذلك بلا معنى الفعل في الحقيقة لجاز الأمر بشيء يكون لأمس أو للعام الأول أو بإنشاء الخلائق، وإن كان لا (١٠) معنى لذلك في أمر الخلق ، ثم في العقل قبيح أن يضاف إلى الله تعالى الطاعة والمعصية، وارتكاب
Clarification of the invalidity of the statement of the Jabriyya. And the doctrine of the Jabriyya is invalid by evidence of scripture, reason, and necessity, which makes the one who repels that a stubborn opponent. As for scripture, it is from verses like: 'Do whatever you will' and 'do good', and regarding recompense: 'Thus Allah shows them their deeds as regrets upon them', and His saying: 'And whoever does an atom's weight', and His saying: 'A recompense for what they used to do', and other than that which established for them the names of workers and for their act the name of act, by command, prohibition, promise, and threat. And there is not in attribution to Allah negation of that; rather, it is that Allah created them upon something and brought them into existence after they were not, and for the creation is what they acquired and did, upon that Allah commanded and prohibited. And it is impossible to command something with no act for the one commanded or prohibited. And Allah said: 'Indeed, Allah commands justice and goodness.' And if commanding with that without a meaning of act in reality were permissible, it would be permissible to command something that occurred yesterday or last year or with creating the universes, even though there is no meaning to that in the command of creation. Then, in reason, it is ugly to attribute obedience and sin to Allah, and committing...
Source pages p. 853

Commentary
This passage refutes the doctrine of the Jabriyya (determinists). The author declares that their view is false by three types of evidence: textual revelation, reason, and necessity, such that anyone who opposes becomes arrogant. First, the textual evidence: Quranic verses command actions (e.g., 'Do whatever you will', 'do good'), and promise reward and punishment based on deeds (e.g., 'Thus Allah shows them their deeds as regrets upon them', 'Whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it', 'A recompense for what they used to do'). These verses clearly attribute actions to servants and use the names 'workers' and 'act' in the context of command, prohibition, promise, and threat. Attributing these actions ultimately to Allah as their Creator does not negate the servant's role; rather, Allah creates them with a basis, and the creation acquires and does them. Second, rational proof: It is impossible to command something if the commanded person has no real ability to perform the commanded (or prohibited) act. If commanding without any real meaning of act were permissible, it would be permissible to command impossible things like something from yesterday or creating universes, which is absurd. Third, reason also deems it ugly to attribute obedience and sin directly to Allah, though the passage breaks off mid-sentence ('and committing...') before completing this point.

الأمر والنهي
الوعد والوعيد
الكسب

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Allah creates all actions, then humans have no responsibility.
Correction: The author explains that Allah creates actions and humans acquire them; the Quranic verses affirm human agency.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following does the scriptural evidence refute?
A) The existence of free will
B) The doctrine of Jabriyya (absolute determinism)
C) The importance of good deeds
D) The possibility of divine command

Key Takeaway
Quranic commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats prove that humans have genuine agency, refuting the Jabriyya doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Quran commands you to do good and avoid evil. What one specific command have you been ignoring, believing it is too hard or that you are not strong enough? If you truly have agency, what are you going to do about it today?
?
Imagine standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment with the deeds you used to do. Given the verses in this passage, what regret would you feel most intensely, and how can you change that starting now?

Rational Refutation: Command Requires Ability
Rational argument against Jabriyya using the impossibility of commanding without ability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that commanding without the ability to act is impossible, thereby refuting the Jabriyya.

Core Idea
Commanding the incapable is logically absurd.

After presenting scriptural evidence, the author offers a rational proof. He argues that divine commands and prohibitions only make sense if the commanded person has the ability to obey or disobey. If not, commanding would be meaningless and lead to absurd consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the rational argument carefully
Read the Arabic from 'ولو جاز الأمر بذلك...' to the end of the passage. Note the author's reasoning.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the main argument is complete.
2
Identify the core principle
The author states: 'It is impossible to command something with no act for the one commanded or prohibited.' This is the key rational principle.
3
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
The author argues: if commanding without ability were allowed, then one could command something from yesterday or create universes—clearly impossible.
This shows the Jabriyya position leads to logical absurdity.
4
Connect to the refutation
Since the Jabriyya deny human ability, they cannot explain why Allah commands and prohibits. Their view collapses.

Refutation of the Jabriyya Claim of Compulsion
Nasafi refutes the Jabriyya using threefold evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Jabriyya doctrine is invalid according to revelation, reason, and necessity.

Core Idea
The Jabriyya view self-destructs: it makes God the doer of sin and eliminates human responsibility.

Imam al-Nasafi presents a decisive refutation of the Jabriyya, who claim humans have no real agency. He draws on three foundations: the clear verses of the Qur'an, rational coherence, and the undeniable human experience of choice. This passage demonstrates that attributing all actions to God alone leads to absurd conclusions unacceptable in both scripture and intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Let the author's own wording set the stage for the arguments that follow.
Notice the rhythm of refutation: declaration, scriptural quotes, rational reasoning, and experiential evidence.
2
Identify the three types of evidence
Nasafi explicitly states the Jabriyya view is invalid by sam' (revelation), 'aql (reason), and darura (necessity). Locate where each begins in the text.
He uses 'Ammā al-sam‘u...', 'Thumma fī al-‘aqli...', and 'Wa-ayḍan anna kulla ḥaddin...'
3
Examine the scriptural proof
Find verses about command, prohibition, reward, and punishment. How do they show that humans have real actions? Note that attributing creation to God does not negate human kash (acquisition).
Key terms: amr, nahy, thawāb, ‘iqāb.
4
Examine the rational proof
Nasafi argues it is qabīḥ (ugly) to attribute sin to God, and impossible for one to command or obey oneself. Trace his logical steps leading to absurd consequences.
He uses 'muḥāl' (impossible) to stress contradiction.
5
Understand the necessity proof and conclusion
Every person knows by intuition they are free and choose their actions. If this knowledge were false, all sensory knowledge would be suspect. Nasafi then notes the Jabriyya sect is extinct, making detailed refutation unnecessary.
The phrase 'wa lā quwwata illā bi-Llāh' punctuates the argument as a reminder of divine power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان بطلان قول الجبرية
ومذهب الجبرية باطل بدلالة السمع والعقل والضرورة التي تصير دافع ذلك مكابرًا. فأما السمع فمن نحو قوله تعالى: اعْمَلُوا مَا شِنْتُمْ وَأَفْعَلُوا الْخَيْرَ، وفي الجزاء: كَذَلِكَ يُرِيهِمُ اللَّهُ أَعْمَلَهُمْ حَسَرَاتٍ عَلَيْهِمْ وقوله تعالى: وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ وقوله: جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ وغير ذلك مما أثبت لهم أسماء الأعمال ولفعلهم اسم الفعل بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، وليس في الإضافة إلى الله تعالى نفي ذلك بل هي الله تعالى بأن خلقها على ما وأوجدها بعد أن لم تكن، وللخلق على ما كسبوها وفعلوها على أن الله تعالى أمر ونهى ومحال الأمر بما لا فعل للمأمور أو المنهى، وقال الله تعالى: إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَأْمُرُ بِالْعَدْلِ وَالْإِحْسَنِ ولو جاز الأمر بذلك بلا معنى الفعل في الحقيقة لجاز الأمر بشيء يكون لأمس أو للعام الأول أو بإنشاء الخلائق، وإن كان لا معنى لذلك في أمر الخلق، ثم في العقل قبيح أن يضاف إلى الله تعالى الطاعة والمعصية، وارتكاب الفواحش والمناكير، وأنه المأمور المنهى المثاب المعاقب، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له ولا قوة إلا بالله وأيضا أن الله تعالى إنما وعد الثواب لمن أطاعه الدنيا والعقاب لمن عصاه فإذا كان الأمران فعله فإذا هو المجزي بما ذكر، وإذا كان الثواب والعقاب حقيقة فالائتمار والانتهاء كذلك، ولا قوة إلا بالله تعالى وكذلك في العقل محال أن يأمر أحد نفسه أو يطيعه أو يعصيه، ومحال تسمية الله تعالى عبدًا ذليلاً مطيعا عاصيًا سفيهًا جائراً، وقد سمى الله تعالى بهذا كله أولئك الذين أمرهم ونهاهم، فإذا صارت هذه الأسماء في التحقيق له فيكون هو الرب وهو العبد وهو الخالق والمخلوق ولا غيره، وذلك مدفوع في السمع والعقل جميعًا، ولا قوة إلا بالله وأيضا أن كل حد يعلم من نفسه أنه مختار لما يفعله، وأنه فاعل كاسب فلو جاز صرف مثله عما هو طريق العلم به الحس أو إبطاله فحق العلم بجميع العالم مثله، وذلك قول مهجور، ومثله قول أهل الجبر، وهذا قول تغني الحكاية عن الإطناب فيه لانقراض الجبرية عن آخرهم وارتفاع مقالتهم، ولما ليس لهذا القول معنى تكلم عليه صاحبه إذ هو ينفي عن نفسه حقيقة كل قول وفعل، وإذا انتفى بطل القول، وبه يناظر ويحاج، فزال الذي يكون به الحجاج واضمحل.
Statement of the invalidity of the Jabriyya's view. And the Jabriyya doctrine is invalid by the indication of revelation, reason, and necessity which makes the repeller of that a stubborn one. As for revelation, from (verses) like His saying, the Most High: 'Do whatever you will and do good', and concerning recompense: 'Thus God shows them their works as regrets upon them' and His saying, the Most High: 'And whoever does an atom's weight' and His saying: 'Recompense for what they used to do' and other than that which established for them the names of actions and for their act the name of the act, with command, prohibition, promise, and threat. And there is not in the attribution to God, the Most High, a negation of that, but (of) God, the Most High, by His creating them as (they are) and bringing them into existence after they were not, and for the creation by their acquisition of them and their doing them, while God, the Most High, commands and prohibits, and it is impossible to command what the commanded or prohibited has no act of. And God, the Most High, said: 'Indeed God commands justice and excellence'. And if it were permissible to command that without a meaning of act in reality, it would be permissible to command something which is for yesterday or for the first year or for the creation of creatures, even if there is no meaning for that in the command of creation. Then, in reason, it is ugly to attribute to God, the Most High, obedience and disobedience, and committing lewdness and abominations, and that He is the commanded, the prohibited, the rewarded, the punished. So it is invalid that the act be from these aspects His, and there is no power except with God. And also that God, the Most High, promised reward in this world to whoever obeys Him and punishment to whoever disobeys Him. So if both matters are His act, then He is the one recompensed for what was mentioned. And if reward and punishment are real, then the obeying and refraining are likewise, and there is no power except with God, the Most High. And likewise, in reason, it is impossible that one command himself or obey him or disobey him, and it is impossible to name God, the Most High, a lowly servant, obedient, disobedient, foolish, unjust. And God, the Most High, named with all of this those whom He commanded and prohibited. So if these names become in reality His, then He is the Lord and He is the servant, and He is the Creator and the created, and no other. And that is repudiated in revelation and reason all together, and there is no power except with God. And also that every individual knows from himself that he is free in what he does, and that he is an agent and acquirer. So if it were permissible to divert someone like him from that which is the way of knowledge by sense or to nullify it, then the truth of knowledge of all the world would be like it. And that is a forsaken saying, and like it is the saying of the people of compulsion. And this is a saying whose narration suffices from elaboration about it due to the extinction of the Jabriyya to the last of them and the disappearance of their doctrine. And since this saying has no meaning, its speaker has spoken upon it, for it negates from itself the reality of every saying and deed. And when it is negated, the saying is invalidated, and by it one argues and disputes, so that by which disputation occurs has vanished and perished.
Source pages p. 853

Commentary
This is a refutation (bayān buṭlān) of the Jabriyya doctrine of absolute compulsion. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, declares their view invalid by three types of evidence: revelation (samʿ), reason (ʿaql), and necessity (ḍarūra), which makes anyone who rejects it a stubborn disputant. He begins with scriptural proofs: verses that command and prohibit actions ('Do whatever you will', 'Do good'), and verses that promise reward and punishment for deeds, as well as verses that call actions by their names. These show that humans have real acts. Attributing actions to God as Creator does not negate this, because God creates the actions and humans acquire them (kasb). It is impossible to command someone who has no capacity to act. He then gives a rational argument: it is absurd to attribute obedience, disobedience, and immoral acts to God, or to call God a servant, sinner, etc. If all actions were from God, then God would be the commanded, prohibited, rewarded, and punished, which contradicts revelation and reason. Moreover, every person knows intuitively (by necessity) that they are free and capable, and if this self-knowledge were false, all sensory knowledge would be invalid. Finally, he notes that the Jabriyya sect is extinct; their view is self-refuting because it denies the reality of all speech and action, and thus collapses on its own terms.

سمع
عقل
ضرورة
كسب
أمر

ثواب
عقاب
فاعل
مختار

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Jabriyya view simply denies free will, without the theological consequence of attributing sin to God.
Correction: Nasafi shows it leads to attributing all actions, including evil, to God, which makes God the servant and sinner.

Checkpoint
Which type of evidence does Nasafi NOT use in refuting the Jabriyya?
A) Revelation (samʿ)
B) Reason (ʿaql)
C) Consensus (ijmāʿ)
D) Necessity (ḍarūra)

Key Takeaway
The Jabriyya doctrine is invalid because it contradicts revelation, reason, and human intuition, and leads to attributing sin to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage argues that every person knows they are free. When you act, do you live as if you are truly accountable, or do you secretly believe you are forced? What would change if you fully owned your choices?
?
If you truly believed that God's commands are given because you can obey, would you dare delay repentance another day? What is stopping you from obeying right now?

The Mu'tazila Argument from 'Ahsan al-Khaliqin'
Nasafi presents the Mu'tazila's first shubha from the Quranic phrase 'Ahsan al-Khaliqin'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's first scriptural proof for human creation of actions based on the Quranic phrase 'Ahsan al-Khaliqin' and the logical structure of their analogy.

Core Idea
A superlative like 'best of creators' implies other creators exist.

The Mu'tazila, known for emphasizing human free will, used Quranic verses to argue that humans truly create their own acts. Their first proof is based on the verse 'So blessed be God, the best of creators' (23:14). Imam Nasafi begins his refutation by presenting this argument fairly. Let's examine how they interpret this verse and why they think it proves human creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the key phrase 'أحسن الخالقين' and the two analogies (the scribe and the impossible 'greatest of gods').
Pay attention to the logical flow: verse → implication → analogies.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila's inference
The Mu'tazila argue that the superlative 'ahsan' (best) only makes sense if there are other creators. Without other creators, the superlative would be meaningless, like 'greatest of gods' (since there is only one God).
This is the core of their proof: superlative implies a class.
3
Analyze the scribe analogy
They compare 'best of creators' to saying 'so-and-so is the most skilled of scribes'. This analogy shows how a superlative functions in everyday language.
Does the analogy hold for divine attributes? Consider the difference between creation (khalq) and acquisition (kasb).
4
Contrast with the 'greatest of gods' phrase
They note that saying 'greatest of gods' is impossible because there is no other god. This contrast highlights that 'best of creators' must imply other creators.
The Maturidi response will later distinguish between literal and figurative application of 'khaliq'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام بيننا وبين المعتزلة فنبدأ ببيان ما لهم من الشبه فنقول: إنهم يحتجون من كتاب الله تعالى كقوله تعالى: فَتَبَارَكَ اللَّهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَلِقِينَ في الآية دلالة كون غيره خالقا لأن إطلاق ذلك يوجب أن له تعالى مزية على كل خالق كما يقال: فلان أحذق الكتاب وأجودهم خطًا. ألا ترى أن القول بأنه تعالى أكبر الآلهة محال لاستحالة ثبوت الإلهية لغيره، وهاهنا لما أطلق هذا دل أن غيره خالق.
And as for the discourse between us and the Muʿtazila, we begin by stating what they have of doubts, and we say: They argue from the Book of God, the Most High, such as His saying, the Most High: 'So blessed be God, the best of creators' (23:14). In the verse is an indication of the existence of another besides Him being a creator, because the unrestricted use of that necessitates that He, the Most High, has superiority over every creator, just as it is said: 'So-and-so is the most skilled of scribes and the most elegant of them in handwriting.' Do you not see that the saying that He, the Most High, is 'the greatest of gods' is impossible because of the impossibility of the existence of divinity for other than Him, and here, when this was used unrestrictedly, it indicates that other than Him is a creator.
Source pages p. 854

Commentary
This passage begins the discussion with the Muʿtazila regarding human acts. Nasafi states that he will first present the doubts (shubah) of the Muʿtazila. The first doubt they raise is from the Qur'anic verse 'So blessed be God, the best of creators' (fa-tabāraka llāhu aḥsanu l-khāliqīn). They argue that the use of the superlative 'best' (aḥsan) implies the existence of other creators, because a superlative only makes sense when there are others to compare. By analogy, when one says 'so-and-so is the most skilled of scribes and the most elegant of them in handwriting', it presupposes other scribes. They contrast this with the phrase 'the greatest of gods' (akbaru l-āliha), which is impossible because there is no other god; the superlative here would be meaningless. Since the Qur'an uses 'aḥsanu l-khāliqīn', it must be that there are other creators besides God. This is the Muʿtazilite proof that humans create their own acts.

Key Terms
شبه
خالق
أحسن الخالقين
مزية
إله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that 'khaliq' (creator) can be applied to humans in the same sense as to God, just as the Mu'tazila argue from this verse.
Correction: The Maturidi view distinguishes between creation (khalq) as bringing something from nothing (exclusive to Allah) and acquisition (kasb) as humans acquiring the actions that Allah creates. The verse's superlative can be understood as a rhetorical emphasis on Allah's unique creativity, not implying literal human creators.

Checkpoint
What analogy do the Mu'tazila use to support their interpretation of 'aḥsanu l-khāliqīn'?
A) The analogy of a king and his subjects
B) The analogy of a scribe and his handwriting
C) The analogy of 'the most skilled of scribes' implying other scribes
D) The analogy of fire and burning

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila argue that the Qur'anic phrase 'best of creators' logically implies the existence of other creators, forming their first scriptural proof for human creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accomplish something significant, do you ever feel like you are the sole creator of that achievement? How does the Mu'tazila's argument that humans create their own acts resonate with your own pride? In what specific area of your life do you need to repent of acting as if you are the 'best creator' rather than God?
?
The superlative 'best of creators' implies other creators—but according to the Maturidi response, only God truly creates. In your daily work, do you attribute your actions to your own power or to God's creation of that action through you? Take a moment to silently acknowledge God as the sole Creator in a task you will do today.
?
If you truly believed that God alone is the Creator of all acts, including your sins, how would your view of your own mistakes change? Would you be quicker to seek His forgiveness and slower to blame others? Commit today to confess one failure as something only God can rectify.

Mu'tazilite Argument from Divine Commands
Mu'tazilite reductio against God creating human acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite logical argument from command, prohibition, promise, and threat against the view that God creates all human acts.

Core Idea
If God creates all acts, He would command Himself — a logical absurdity.

This passage presents a key Mu'tazilite objection to the Ash'ari doctrine of acquisition. The Mu'tazilites argue that God's commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats presuppose human agency; if God were the sole creator of acts, these would become self-referential and meaningless. Read carefully to see how they derive a reductio ad absurdum.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the Mu'tazilite argument unfold naturally.
2
Follow the logical chain
Identify the premise: God has given commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats. The conclusion: if God creates all acts, then He would be commanding and prohibiting Himself, making Him the believer and disbeliever. This is absurd.
Notice how the argument extends to blame/praise and punishment/reward.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the Mu'tazilites conclude that such a view leads to unbelief. Think about what this argument reveals about their concept of human agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتعلقون أيضا بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد الثابتة من الله تعالى للناس في أفعال مختلفة، ولو كان الله تعالى هو الذي تولى تخليق أفعالهم وإيجادها لصار أمراً نفسه ناهيًا إياه واعدًا إياه موعدًا إياه لأنه هو الذي تولى إيجادها، فكان هو المؤمن والكافر والمطيع والعاص، وذا محال من تفوه به يحكم بانسلاخه عن الدين. وكذا الذم والمدح على ما يذم ويمدح عليه من الأفعال يكونان راجعين إليه لأن الموجد بذلك أولى ممن ليس بموجد. وكذا التعذيب والإثابة يحصلان على فعل نفسه وهما مقابلان بالفعل، فينبغي أن يكون الله تعالى هو المعاقب المثاب لا العبد، والقول به كفر.
And they also cling to the command, prohibition, promise, and threat established from God Almighty for people concerning various acts. If God Almighty were the one who undertook the creation of their acts and their bringing into existence, then He would become one commanding Himself, prohibiting Himself, promising Himself, and threatening Himself, because He is the one who undertook their bringing into existence. So He would be the believer, the disbeliever, the obedient, and the disobedient. This is impossible; whoever utters it is judged to have stripped himself of religion. Similarly, blame and praise upon the acts that are blamed and praised would revert to Him, because the one who brings into existence is more worthy of that than one who does not bring into existence. Likewise, punishment and reward occur upon His own act, and they are both corresponding to the act. So it should be that God Almighty is the one punished and rewarded, not the slave. And saying this is unbelief.
Source pages p. 855

Commentary
This passage presents a Mu'tazilite argument against the Ash'ari position that God creates all human acts. The Mu'tazilites argue that because God has established commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats for people regarding various acts, if God were the sole creator of those acts, He would be commanding and prohibiting Himself. Consequently, He would be the believer and disbeliever, which is absurd. Furthermore, blame and praise for acts would revert to God, not humans, and punishment and reward would be for God's own acts. The Mu'tazilites conclude that such a view leads to unbelief.

Key Terms
الأمر
النهي
الوعد
الوعيد
تخليق أفعال العباد
الذم
المدح
التعذيب
الإثابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument denies God's power over human actions.
Correction: The argument does not deny God's power; it points out a logical inconsistency between God's attributes of commanding and being the sole creator of the commanded acts.

Checkpoint
What does the Mu'tazilite argue would happen if God creates all human acts?
A) God would be unjust.
B) God would be commanding and prohibiting Himself.
C) Humans would be free from responsibility.
D) Both A and B.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilites used God's own commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats to argue that God cannot be the sole creator of human acts, otherwise those divine attributes would become self-referential and absurd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'It was written for me' to soften the blow? How does this Mu'tazilite argument force you to confront that evasion? Will you take full ownership of your next disobedience, or will you hide behind qadar?
?
If God truly commanded you to do something and you failed, whose failure is it? This passage says God cannot be the one failing because that would make His command self-directed. Does that realization make you tremble at your own responsibility? What will you change today to honor that trust?
?
Picture yourself standing before God on Judgment Day, being asked about your actions. If you had believed God created your sin, would you blame Him? This argument says that is unbelief. Do you have any hidden resentment toward God for your struggles? Will you repent of that and embrace your own agency?

Mu'tazilite Division of Human Acts
Mu'tazilite division of possibilities for human act origin with poetic summary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite three-way division of the origin of human acts and their logical reasoning for attributing acts solely to the slave.

Core Idea
Human acts must originate from one of three sources; only one is logically sound.

The Mu'tazilites used logical division to argue that humans create their own acts. This passage presents their three possibilities and rules out all but one, concluding that the slave is the sole creator. Al-Nashi then versifies the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical structure of the division.
2
Identify the three divisions
The passage presents three possibilities for the origin of a human act: (1) God alone creates it, (2) God and the slave create it together, (3) the slave alone creates it. Find each one in the text.
3
Follow the reasoning for rejecting the first two
The first division is rejected because praise and blame would revert to God. The second is rejected because blame would still revert to the slave, and if it reverted to God, that would be absurd.
The argument relies on the principle that moral responsibility requires being the creator of the act.
4
Understand the conclusion and the poem
The third division is determined: the slave alone creates his acts. Then read al-Nashi's poem, which summarizes the argument in verse.
The poem reinforces the logical elimination of the first two possibilities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقرروا هذا الكلام وأبرزوه على طريقة الاستقراء واشتغلوا بالتقسيم وقالوا فعل العبد لا يخلو إما أن يكون كله من الله تعالى تولى إيجاده بلا صنع (من العبد) وإما أن يكون العبد أوجده أيضا مع الله تعالى فوجد بإيجاد الله تعالى وإيجاد العبد، وقد شارك العبد الله تعالى في إيجاده، وإما أن كان العبد هو الذي تولى الإيجاد على سبيل الانفراد والاستقلال والاستبداد. والقسم الأول فاسد لعود المدح والذم على هذه الأفعال إلى العبد دون الله ولو كان الله تعالى هو الموجد له لرجع إليه الذم والمدح والقسم الثاني أيضا باطل لعود كل الذم على ذلك إلى العبد دون الله تعالى، ولو كان الأمر على ذلك لم يكن العبد بأولى به من الله تعالى فتعين القسم الثالث. ونظم الناشي هذا المعنى فقال: لا تعدو أفعالنا التي نذم بها إحدى ثلاث خلال حين نحصيها إما تفرد مولانا بصنعته فيسقط اللوم عنا حين نأتيها أو كان يشركنا فاللوم يلحقه إن كان يلحقنا من لاتم فيها أو لم يكن للإله في خليقته صنع فما الذنب إلا ذنب جانيها
And they established this discourse and presented it in the manner of induction and engaged in division. They said: The act of the slave is not free from one of three: either it is entirely from God Almighty—He alone undertakes its bringing into existence without any action from the slave; or the slave also brings it into existence together with God Almighty, so it comes into existence by God's bringing into existence and the slave's bringing into existence, and the slave has shared with God Almighty in its bringing into existence; or the slave is the one who undertakes the bringing into existence completely alone, independently, and exclusively. The first division is invalid because praise and blame for these acts revert to the slave, not to God; and if God Almighty were the one who brings it into existence, then blame and praise would revert to Him. The second division is also invalid because all blame for that reverts to the slave, not to God Almighty; and if the matter were so, then the slave would not be more entitled to it than God Almighty. So the third division is determined. And al-Nashi composed poetry on this meaning, saying: 'Our acts for which we are blamed are not beyond one of three traits when we enumerate them: either our Lord alone has the making of it, then blame is removed from us when we bring them; or He shares with us, then blame attaches to Him if blame attaches to us for something faulty; or God has no making in His creation, so the sin is only the sin of its committer.'
Source pages p. 855

Commentary
This passage presents a Mu'tazilite three-way division of possibilities for the origin of human acts. The three possibilities are: (1) God alone creates the act; (2) both God and the slave create; (3) the slave alone creates. They rule out (1) because praise and blame would revert to God, which is absurd. They rule out (2) because blame would still revert to the slave, and if it reverted to God, that would be equally absurd. Therefore, only (3) remains: the slave is the sole creator of his acts. Al-Nashi then summarizes this argument in verse, emphasizing that if God creates alone, we are not blamed; if He shares, blame goes to Him; if He has no part, then only the doer is guilty.

Key Terms
التقسيم
القسم الأول
القسم الثاني
القسم الثالث
الانفراد
الاستقلال
الاستبداد
الناشي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The three divisions are exhaustive but not necessarily valid if one accepts a different definition of 'creation' (e.g., God as ultimate cause).
Correction: The Mu'tazilites insist that moral responsibility requires direct creation of the act, so if God creates, He would be morally accountable. They reject alternative definitions of creation that might allow God to be the ultimate cause while still holding the slave responsible.

Checkpoint
What conclusion do the Mu'tazilites draw from the three divisions?
A) That God creates all acts.
B) That the slave is the sole creator of his acts.
C) That both God and slave create.
D) That acts are uncaused.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilites conclude that only the slave creating his own acts allows for meaningful moral responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'Allah made me do it' or 'It was my destiny'? After reading this passage, how does the Mu'tazilite rejection of the first two divisions force you to confront that excuse?
?
If you truly believed that your actions are entirely your own creation—independent of any divine input—how would that affect the sincerity of your repentance? Would you feel more desperate for mercy or more self-reliant?
?
The Mu'tazilites argue that moral blame cannot fall on God because it would be unjust. Yet have you ever, in a moment of hardship, blamed Allah for your own mistakes? What does this passage teach you about the relationship between your free will and your accountability before Him?

The Mu'tazilite Argument Against Dual Agency
Mu'tazilite argument that dual agency entails shirk, compulsion, or incapacitating God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite reductio ad absurdum argument against the view that both God and humans create actions, and why they consider such dual agency impossible.

Core Idea
Dual agency leads to shirk or absurdity, so it must be false.

The Mu'tazilites argued that if humans genuinely share in the creation of their acts alongside God, this leads to untenable consequences. They presented a brief but powerful argument showing that such dual agency either makes humans partners with God—a clear violation of tawhid—or forces us into other contradictions. This passage lays out that argument in a dense form, inviting us to see why the Mu'tazilites insisted on human exclusive agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Let the rhythm of the original argument sink in before analyzing.
Notice how the author uses 'وكذا' (similarly) to connect to the previous argument.
2
Identify the two consequences
The passage lists two main consequences of dual agency. First, it leads to making servants partners with God (shirk). Second, it leads to compulsion or incapacitation of God. Identify these clearly.
The second consequence is presented as an alternative: either compulsion or incapacitation, both problematic.
3
Understand the logic of impossibility
The passage states that both consequences are 'clearly corrupt in their impossibility' and that whatever leads to impossibility is itself impossible. Follow the logical chain: if premise P leads to Q, and Q is impossible, then P is impossible.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum. The Mu'tazilites assume the opponent's view leads to absurdities, thus the view must be rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا القول به يؤدي إلى جعل العباد شركاء الله تعالى في تحصيل الأفعال، لأنها تحصل بقدرته تعالى وبقدرتهم، والقول بإثبات الشريك الله تعالى في تخليق العالم كفر صراح، وخروج عن التوحيد إلى القول بالتثنية، وكذا القول به يؤدي إلى أن يكون العباد مضطرين في أفعالهم أو يؤدي إلى تعجيز الله تعالى، وكلا الأمرين بين الإحالة ظاهر الفساد، وما أدى إلى ما هو المحال كان محالاً ممتنعا في نفسه.
Similarly, holding this view leads to making the servants partners with God Almighty in effecting acts, because they occur by His power and by their power. And saying that a partner is established for God Almighty in the creation of the world is outright unbelief, and a departure from monotheism to the saying of dualism. Similarly, holding this view leads to the servants being compelled in their acts, or it leads to incapacitating God Almighty. Both matters are clearly corrupt in their impossibility. And whatever leads to what is impossible is itself impossible and forbidden.
Source pages p. 856

Commentary
This passage presents two further consequences that the Mu'tazilites derive from the opposing view (that both God and human have power over the act). First, it leads to making humans partners with God in creation, which is shirk and dualism. Second, it either implies that humans are compelled (which contradicts justice) or that God is incapacitated (which is impossible). Since both consequences are impossible, the premise that God shares power with humans must be false. Therefore, only the position that humans are the sole creators of their acts remains valid.

Key Terms
الشرك
الشريك
التثنية
الاضطرار
تعجيز الله
الإحالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilite argument, what does holding that both God and human create the act lead to?
A) Justice of God.
B) Shirk or compulsion.
C) Free will.
D) Predestination.

Key Takeaway
Dual agency is impossible because it leads to either shirk or compulsion and incapacity of God—all of which are unacceptable in Islamic theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something, do you genuinely feel that your efforts were created by God and you merely acquired them, or do you sense a self-sufficiency that contradicts tawhid? How can you train yourself to immediately attribute all causation to Allah alone?
?
The Mu'tazilites argue that any sharing of power in creation is shirk. How often do you unconsciously attribute a success to your own skill or effort without immediately recognizing that Allah created both the action and its outcome? Will you commit to saying 'MashaAllah' and reminding yourself of Allah's sole power every time you feel a sense of personal achievement?
?
This lesson shows that any view leading to impossibility must be rejected. Are there beliefs or habits in your life that logically lead to absurd consequences regarding Allah's attributes (such as limiting His power or associating partners)? What is one such belief you need to uproot today?
